The Ash'ari Criterion: Negation and Its Contrary
Ash'ari criterion for distinguishing essential and active attributes with application to will and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ariyya distinguish attributes of essence from attributes of act based on whether negating the attribute necessitates a contrary.

Core Idea
An attribute is essential if negating it entails its opposite; otherwise it is an act.

Having presented the Mu'tazila view, the author now turns to the Ash'ari position. Unlike the Mu'tazila, the Ash'ariyya focus on logical entailment: if negating an attribute forces the existence of its opposite, that attribute must be eternal. This lesson explores their reasoning, especially how they argue that will and speech are essential despite being relational.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari criterion
The Ash'ariyya state that if negating an attribute implies its contrary, the attribute is essential. Otherwise it is an act.
2
Examine the examples
Examples: life (negation → death) is essential; creating (negation does not imply a specific opposite) is an act.
3
Apply to will and speech
The Ash'ariyya argue that negating will implies compulsion and negating speech implies dumbness, so they are essential.
This is a key point of difference from the Mu'tazila.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفعلية أي الصفات الفعلية، وهي التي يتوقف ظهورها على وجود الخلق، اعلم أن بين صفات الذات وصفات الفعل مختلف فيه. فعند المعتزلة ما جرى فيه النفي والإثبات فهو من صفات الفعل، كما يقال : خلق لفلان ولداً ولم يخلق لفلان، ورزق لزيد مالاً ولم يرزق لعمرو، وما لا يجري فيه النفي فهو من صفات الذات كالعلم والقدرة فلا يقال : لم يعلم كذا ولم يقدر على كذا فالإرادة والكلام مما يجري فيه النفي والإثبات، قال الله تعالى: يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ [البقرة: ١٨٥]، ﴿ وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسى تَكْلِيمًا ﴾ [النساء: ١٦٤]، وَلَا : يُكَلِّمُهُمُ الله يَوْمَ الْقِيِّمَةِ [البقرة: ١٧٤]، فكانا من صفات الفعل وكانا حادثين. وأما عند الأشعرية فالفرق بينهما أن ما يلزم من نفيه نقيضه فهو من صفات الذات، فإنك لو نفيت الحياة يلزم الموت، ولو نفيت القدرة يلزم العجز وكذا العلم مع الجهل، وما لا يلزم من نفيه نقيضه فهو من صفات الفعل، فلو نفيت الإحياء أو الإماتة أو الخلق أو الرزق لم يلزم منه نقيضه، فعلى هذا الحد لو نفيت الإرادة لزم منه الجبر والاضطرار، ولو نفيت عنه الكلام لزم الخرس والسكوت، فثبت أنهما من صفات الذات. وعندنا أن كل ما وصف به ولا يجوز أن يوصف بضده فهو من صفات الذات، كالقدرة والعلم والعزّة والعظمة، وكل ما يجوز أن يوصف به وبضده فهو من صفات الفعل كالرأفة والرحمة والسخط والغضب.
As for the active attributes, i.e., the attributes of act, which are those whose manifestation depends on the existence of creation. Know that there is disagreement regarding the distinction between attributes of essence and attributes of act. According to the Mu'tazila, what admits of affirmation and negation is from the attributes of act, as is said: He created for someone a child and did not create for another, and He provided for Zayd wealth and did not provide for Amr; and what does not admit of affirmation and negation is from the attributes of essence, like knowledge and power, so it is not said: He did not know such-and-such and He was not able to do such-and-such. Thus will and speech are among what admit of affirmation and negation. Allah the Exalted said: 'Allah desires ease for you and does not desire hardship for you' [2:185], and 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' [4:164], and 'And He will not speak to them on the Day of Resurrection' [2:174]; thus they are from attributes of act and are originated. And according to the Ash'ariyya, the difference between them is that whatever negation entails its contrary is from attributes of essence; for if you negate life, death follows, and if you negate power, incapacity follows, and likewise knowledge with ignorance; and whatever negation does not entail its contrary is from attributes of act; if you negate giving life or causing death or creating or providing, no contrary follows from it. According to this criterion, if you negate will, compulsion and constraint follow, and if you negate speech from Him, dumbness and silence follow; thus it is established that they are from attributes of essence. And according to us: whatever He is described with and it is not permissible to describe Him with its opposite is from attributes of essence, like power, knowledge, might, and greatness; and whatever it is permissible to describe Him with and with its opposite is from attributes of act, like compassion, mercy, displeasure, and anger.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a classification and comparative analysis of the distinction between attributes of essence (sifat al-dhat) and attributes of act (sifat al-fi'l). The author begins by defining attributes of act as those whose manifestation depends on creation. He then presents three positions. First, the Mu'tazila: they say that any attribute that can be affirmed or negated of Allah (like creating, providing, willing, speaking) is an attribute of act, and thus originated (hadith). They support this by noting that we can say 'He created' or 'He did not create', and similarly for will and speech; they cite verses where will and speech are affirmed or negated. Second, the Ash'ariyya hold that the criterion is whether negation necessitates a contrary (did). For example, negating life necessarily implies death, so life is essential; but negating an act like giving life does not imply its opposite (taking life is not a necessary opposite, because one could simply not give life). Applying this to will and speech, negating will implies compulsion (jabr) which is a deficiency, so will is essential; negating speech implies dumbness, so speech is essential. Third, the author states 'according to us' (Maturidi school): the criterion is whether it is permissible to describe Allah by both an attribute and its opposite. If not permissible (e.g., power and inability), it is essential; if permissible (e.g., mercy and anger), it is an attribute of act. Thus, will and speech are essential because one cannot attribute inability or silence to Allah, whereas mercy and anger are active because He can show mercy or anger.

Key Terms
الأشعرية
نقيض
صفات الذات
صفات الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because will and speech involve relation to creation, they must be attributes of act.
Correction: The Ash'ariyya show that negating them leads to a deficiency, so they are essential.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ariyya, why is will an attribute of essence?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran.
B) Negating it implies compulsion.
C) It can be affirmed and negated.
D) It is not related to creation.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ariyya prioritize logical entailment: an attribute is essential if its negation forces a specific opposite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Ash'ari criterion shows that negating Allah's will leads to compulsion (jabr). Do you truly believe that everything in your life, even your choices, is under His will, or do you sometimes feel that your free will is independent of Him? How does this truth change your perspective on your decisions today? What one step will you take to surrender more fully to His will?
?
Reflect on an area of your life where you attribute 'dumbness' or 'silence' to Allah—perhaps a prayer you think He didn't answer. If you believe His speech is essential and perfect, how does that reshape your understanding of His silence? What one step will you take to trust His wisdom instead of demanding an answer?
?
The lesson declares that negating Allah's power entails incapacity. Do you live as if Allah is powerful over all things, or do you secretly think some problems are too big for Him? What concrete change in your reliance on Him can you make starting today—perhaps in a specific worry you've been carrying?

The Maturidi Criterion: Permissibility of Opposite Description
Maturidi criterion distinguishing attributes based on permissibility of opposite description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi school distinguishes attributes of essence from attributes of act: an attribute is essential if it is impermissible to describe Allah with its opposite.

Core Idea
If Allah cannot be described by the opposite of an attribute, that attribute is essential.

Finally, the author presents his own school's position, which is the Maturidi view. They propose a different criterion: rather than focusing on negation or entailment, they look at whether it is possible to attribute the opposite to Allah. For example, Allah cannot be described as weak or ignorant, so power and knowledge are essential. But He can be described as both merciful and angry, so those are attributes of act.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi criterion
The author states: whatever Allah is described with and it is not permissible to describe Him with its opposite is an attribute of essence.
2
Examine the examples
Essential attributes: power, knowledge, might, greatness. Active attributes: compassion, mercy, displeasure, anger.
3
Apply the criterion
Test other attributes: e.g., will (opposite compulsion cannot be attributed) so essential; speech (opposite silence cannot be attributed) so essential.
This criterion is simpler than the Ash'ari one.

?

?

What would change in your worship if you took His anger as seriously as His mercy?
?

How does recognizing that actions like mercy or anger depend on His will shape your supplication? Will you now call upon Allah by all His names, including Al-Ghadab (The Angry), with the same reverence as Ar-Rahman (The Merciful)?

Defending the Eternity of Takwin: Objection and Answer
The author presents an objection and refutes it with multiple arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends the eternity of the divine attribute takwin (bringing into existence) against the objection that an eternal attribute would necessitate an eternal effect.

Core Idea
Eternal takwin produces temporal effects, just as eternal knowledge knows temporal things.

This passage is a classic kalam dialectical exchange. The opponent argues that if takwin is eternal, then its effect must also be eternal, which is impossible because the world is temporal; therefore takwin must be temporal. The author refutes this by showing that the opponent's alternative leads to absurdities like infinite regress or negation of God's action, and then provides a positive argument: takwin is eternal but its relation to the created thing is temporal, analogous to eternal knowledge of temporal objects.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to how the opponent's objection is set up and how the author begins to answer it.
The objection states that an eternal takwin would require an eternal created thing.
2
Analyze the three options in the answer
The author presents three possibilities if takwin were temporal: infinite regress, an eternal takwin, or no takwin at all. Identify these and see why only the second is acceptable.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
3
Examine the analogy with knowledge
The author compares takwin to knowledge: eternal knowledge can have temporal objects. Consider how this analogy supports the eternity of takwin.
This shows that an eternal attribute can relate to temporal things.
4
Follow the dialectical exchange
Read the part beginning with 'Then we say to them' and trace the questions and answers. See how the author forces the opponent into a contradiction.
This exchange deepens the argument by considering the world's relation to God's essence or attributes.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that the author's position is that takwin is eternal and its effect (al-mukawwan) is temporal, and that this is consistent with divine attributes and avoids the opponent's pitfalls.
This lesson shows a sophisticated use of logic in theology.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالتخليق والترزيق والإنشاء والإبداع والصنع وغير ذلك من صفات الفعل، [؟...؟] الأزل، ولو تعلق بوجوده في الأزل لوجب وجود المكون فى الأزل؛ لأن القول بالتكوين ولا مكون كالقول بالضرب ولا مضروب وأنه محال فلابد أن يكون التكوين حادثا. والجواب: أن التكوين إن حدث بالتكوين فهو تكوين محتاج إلى تكوين فيؤدي إلى التسلسل وهو باطل أو ينتهي إلى تكوين قديم وهو الذي ندعيه أو لا بتكوين أحد ففيه تعطيل الصانع. والحاصل أنا نقول : التكوين قديم والمتعلق به هو المكون وهو حادث، كما أن العلم قديم وبعض المعلومات حادث على أن التكوين في الأزل لم يكن ليكون العالم به في الأزل بل ليكون وقت وجوده، فتكوينه باق أبدا، فيتعلق وجود كل موجود بتكوينه الأزلي، بخلاف الضرب؛ لأنه عرض، فلا يتصور بقاؤه إلى وقت وجود المضروب، ثم نقول لهم: هل تعلق وجود العالم بذاته أو بصفة من صفاته أم لا ؟ فإن قالوا: لا عطلوه، وإن قالوا: نعم، قلنا فما تعلق به أزلي أم حادث؟ فإن قالوا: حادث فهو من العالم وكان تعلق حدوث العالم ببعض منه لا به تعالى وفيه تعطيله وإن قالوا أزلي، قلنا: هل اقتضى ذلك أزلية العالم أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، كفروا، وإن قالوا: لا، بطلت شبهتم على أن تعلق وجود العالم بخطاب كن عند الأشعري فكان تكويناً وهو أزلي فيكون مناقضا.
So takhliq, tarziq, insha', ibda', san', and other attributes of action, [؟...؟] eternity, and if it were related to its existence in eternity then the existence of the created thing (al-mukawwan) would be necessary in eternity; because saying 'bringing into existence (takwin) without that which is brought into existence' is like saying 'striking without that which is struck' and that is impossible, so bringing into existence must be temporal. And the answer: that if bringing into existence occurs by [another] bringing into existence, then that bringing into existence is in need of a bringing into existence, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul), which is false; or it ends with an eternal bringing into existence, which is what we claim; or it occurs without any bringing into existence, which entails the negation of the Creator (ta'til). The upshot is that we say: Bringing into existence (takwin) is eternal, and that which it is related to (al-mukawwan) is temporal, just as knowledge is eternal while some known things are temporal. Moreover, bringing into existence in eternity was not such that the world would exist in eternity, but rather [it was] for the time of its existence. So His bringing into existence remains forever, so the existence of every existing thing is related to His eternal bringing into existence, unlike striking because it is an accident ('arad), so its continuance until the time of the existence of that which is struck is inconceivable. Then we say to them: Is the existence of the world related to His Essence (dhat) or to one of His attributes or not? If they say: No, they have negated [His action]. If they say: Yes, we say: Is that which it is related to eternal or temporal? If they say: temporal, then it is part of the world, and the temporal occurrence of the world would be related to some part of it, not to Him, may He be exalted, and in that is negation of Him (ta'til). And if they say: eternal, we say: Did that necessitate the eternity of the world or not? If they say: Yes, they have disbelieved (kafaru). If they say: No, their doubt is invalidated, given that the existence of the world is related to the address 'Be' (kun) according to al-Ash'ari, which was takwin and is eternal, so [their position] would be contradictory.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer regarding the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The opponent argues: if takwin is eternal, then its object (the created thing) would have to be eternal because an eternal attribute cannot have a temporal effect; this is like saying 'striking without a struck object' is impossible. Therefore takwin must be temporal. The answer refutes this by showing that takwin, if temporal, would require another takwin leading to infinite regress, or else one ends with an eternal takwin (the author's position), or else no takwin at all (which negates God's action). So takwin is eternal while its effect is temporal, analogous to knowledge which is eternal but many known things are temporal. Furthermore, takwin in eternity was not intended to create the world in eternity but to bring it into existence at its proper time. The author then extends the argument into a dialectical exchange: the opponent is asked whether the world's existence relates to God's essence or attribute. If they say no, they negate God's action; if yes, that relation must be either eternal or temporal. Temporal leads to part of the world being the cause of itself; eternal leads to the world being eternal, which is disbelief. Thus the opponent's position collapses.

الحادث

التعطيل

الضرب
العرض

كُن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An eternal attribute cannot produce a temporal effect.
Correction: The author shows that takwin is eternal but its effect is temporal, just as eternal knowledge encompasses temporal objects. The attribute's eternity does not necessitate the eternity of its object.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the relationship between takwin and the created thing (al-mukawwan)?
A) Both are eternal.
B) Takwin is eternal while al-mukawwan is temporal.
C) Takwin is temporal while al-mukawwan is eternal.
D) Both are temporal.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of takwin is eternal, and its effect is temporal; this is consistent with divine attributes and avoids logical absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your very existence is due to an eternal act of takwin from God, how does that change the weight and meaning of your daily choices? Are you living as if each moment is a direct result of that eternal command, or do you take your existence for granted?
?
The author argues that denying God's eternal attribute of takwin leads to 'ta'til'—making God inactive. In your own life, where have you subtly acted as if God's power is limited or disconnected from the world, perhaps by relying solely on material causes without acknowledging His direct, ongoing role?
?
If God's eternal takwin 'remains forever' and every created thing is linked to that single eternal act, then nothing is outside His will. Is there an area of your life where you resist submitting to His decree, as if that area were somehow independent of His eternal bringing into existence?

All Action Attributes Reduce to Takwin
Listing action attributes, reducing them to takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school holds that all divine action attributes are reducible to the single eternal attribute of takwin.

Core Idea
All divine action attributes are expressions of one attribute: takwin.

In this passage, the author lists several action attributes such as creating, providing sustenance, and giving life, and argues that they are all included under the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). He contrasts this view with al-Ash'ari's relational view and the Transoxianan multiplication view, offering a middle path that preserves the unity of God's eternal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of action attributes
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the list of attributes: takhliq, tarziq, insha', ibda', san', ihya', ifna', inbat, inma', taswir.
Notice how the author groups them under 'other attributes of action'.
2
Understand the two opposing views
Identify the views of al-Ash'ari (action attributes are relational) and some Transoxianan scholars (each is a real eternal attribute). Understand why the author rejects both.
Al-Ash'ari's view lessens reality; the Transoxianan view multiplies eternal entities.
3
Grasp the reduction to takwin
See how the author argues that all action attributes are actually takwin, named differently based on the object. For example, takwin related to life is called ihya'.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
Consider why this matters: it preserves the unity and simplicity of God's attributes while accounting for diverse acts.

فالتخليق والترزيق وهو خلق الأشياء ورزق الأشياء والإنشاء) أي الإبداء والإبداع) أي اختراع الأشياء والصنع) أي إظهاره بإظهار المصنوعات في حال الابتداء (وغير ذلك من صفات (الفعل كالإحياء والإفناء والإنبات والإنماء وتصوير الأشياء، والكل داخل تحت صفة التكوين؟ فالصفات الأزلية عندنا ثمانية لا كما زعم الأشعري من أن الصفات الفعلية إضافات، ولا كما تفرد به بعض علماء ما وراء النهر بكون كل من الصفات الفعلية صفة حقيقية أزلية، فإن فيه تكثير القدماء جداً وإن لم تكن متغايرة؟ فالأولى أن يقال: إن مرجع الكل إلى التكوين فإنه إن تعلق بالحياة يسمى إحياء وبالموت إماتة وبالصورة تصويرا إلى غير ذلك فالكل تكوين وإنما الخصوص بخصوصيات المتعلقات.
So takhliq (creating) and tarziq (providing sustenance) – which is creating things and providing sustenance for things – and insha' (originating) – meaning ibda' (innovating) – meaning inventing things – and san' (making) – meaning manifesting it by manifesting made things in the state of beginning – and other attributes of action, such as giving life (ihya'), giving death (ifna'), causing growth (inbat), causing development (inma'), and forming things (taswir), and all are included under the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence)? The eternal attributes with us are eight, not as al-Ash'ari claimed that the attributes of action are relational (idafat), nor as some scholars beyond the river (ma wara' al-nahr) uniquely held that each of the attributes of action is a real eternal attribute, for in that there is a great multiplication of eternal entities, even if they are not distinct? So the best is to say: The reference of all is to takwin, for if it relates to life it is called giving life (ihya'), to death giving death (imata), to form giving form (taswir), and so on. So all are takwin, and the specification is only due to the specificities of the objects.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage classifies the action attributes. The author lists several: takhliq (creating), tarziq (providing sustenance), insha' (originating), ibda' (innovating), san' (making), and others like ihya' (giving life), ifna' (giving death), inbat (causing growth), inma' (causing development), taswir (forming). He asserts that all are included under the attribute of takwin. He then contrasts his position with two others: al-Ash'ari considered these attributes merely relational (idafat) and not real; some Transoxianan scholars each as a real eternal attribute, which would multiply eternal entities excessively. The author's preferred view is that all reduce to the single attribute of takwin, which receives different names according to the particular object it relates to (life, death, form, etc.). Thus the specification is due to the specificities of the objects, not a multiplication of attributes.

The Unity of Divine Creative Act (Takwin)
The author argues that all creative terms reduce to takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all divine creative terms (takhliq, insha', fi'l, san', tarziq) ultimately refer to the single attribute of takwin (bringing into being), and their specific names arise from the objects of that act.

Core Idea
All divine creative acts are one attribute: takwin.

The author addresses a potential concern about multiplying eternal attributes. He explains that terms like giving life, causing death, and forming are not separate attributes but specific manifestations of the single attribute takwin. This lesson establishes the foundational unity of Allah's creative act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's opening concern about multiplication of attributes.
Pay attention to the question mark after 'متغايرة' in the Arabic.
2
Identify the author's resolution
The author states that all terms refer to takwin. Find the sentence that says 'فالكل تكوين' and understand its implication.
This is the key unifying statement.
3
Understand the specialization
The author explains how takwin gets specific names based on the object: life, death, form. Reflect on how this preserves the oneness of the attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن فيه تكثير القدماء جداً وإن لم تكن متغايرة؟ فالأولى أن يقال: إن مرجع الكل إلى التكوين فإنه إن تعلق بالحياة يسمى إحياء وبالموت إماتة وبالصورة تصويرا إلى غير ذلك فالكل تكوين وإنما الخصوص بخصوصيات المتعلقات. ثم المتبادر أن معنى التخليق والإنشاء والفعل والصنع واحد وهو إحداث الشيء بعد أن لم يكن، سواء كان على نهج مثال سابق أو لا والصحيح أن لها معاني متقاربة، فإن الإبداع إحداث الشيء بعد أن لم يكن لا على مثال سبق، بخلاف التخليق فإنه أعم منه أو مقابله في التحقيق، والإنشاء يختص بأول الأشياء والفعل كناية عن كل عمل متعد يكون في الخير والشر، والصنع عمل فيه إحكام وحسن نظام كما أشار إليه قوله سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿ صُنْعَ اللَّهِ الَّذِي أَتْقَنَ كُلّ شَيْء [النمل: ۸۸] ، وأما الترزيق فهو إحداث رزق الشيء وجعله قوتا له.
For it contains a great multiplication of the eternal attributes, even if they are not different? So the best is to say: The reference of all of them is to takwin (bringing into being), for if it is related to life it is called ihya (giving life), and to death imata (causing death), and to form taswir (forming), and so on. So all is takwin, and the specificity is only by the specificities of the objects of relation. Then the apparent understanding is that the meaning of takhliq (creation), insha' (origination), fi'l (act), and san' (making) is one, namely bringing something into existence after it had not been, whether or not it was upon a prior pattern. And the correct view is that they have similar meanings. For ibda' (absolute creation) is bringing something into existence after it had not been, without a prior example, unlike takhliq which is more general or its opposite in reality. And insha' is specific to the first of things. And fi'l is a metonym for every transitive act, whether good or evil. And san' is an act in which there is firmness and good order, as indicated by His statement, exalted is He: 'The handiwork of Allah, who has perfected everything' (27:88). And as for tarziq (providing sustenance), it is bringing into existence the provision of something and making it a sustenance for it.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition of the various terms used for Allah's creative acts. The author begins by noting a potential concern about multiplying eternal attributes. He then states that all such terms ultimately refer to takwin (bringing into being). He explains that takwin, when related to specific objects, takes specific names like ihya (giving life), imata (causing death), and taswir (forming). So the diversity is due to the diversity of the objects, not the attribute itself. Next, he examines the apparent meanings of takhliq, insha', fi'l, and san'. He notes that they all fundamentally mean bringing something into existence from non-existence. The correct view is that they have similar but nuanced meanings. He defines ibda' as creation without a prior example, contrasting it with takhliq which is more general. Insha' is especially for the first instances of things. Fi'l is a general term for any transitive action. San' implies skill and order, citing the Quranic verse from Surat an-Naml. Finally, he defines tarziq as providing sustenance to a creature.

تكوين
إحياء
إماتة
تصوير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Creating, giving life, and causing death are separate eternal attributes in Allah.
Correction: They are all manifestations of the single attribute takwin.

Checkpoint

A) They are completely different attributes
B) They all ultimately refer to takwin, with specific names based on the object
C) They are synonyms with no difference
D) Takwin is a derived attribute from takhliq

Key Takeaway
All divine creative terms refer to the single attribute takwin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for a newborn baby, do you ask Allah for 'life' as if it were a separate act, or do you see it as a manifestation of His single, perfect attribute of bringing into being? How must you realign your heart to worship the one Creator behind all outcomes?
?
You have witnessed death and life countless times. Have you ever paused to realize that both are the same divine act, merely related to different objects? Does that unity make you trust Allah's wisdom more deeply, or does it challenge you to see His hand in every moment?
?
If you truly believed that all creative terms—giving life, causing death, forming—are only one attribute, would your gratitude and patience change when facing trials? Commit today to reminding yourself, at least once daily, that every event is from the same single, perfect act of your Lord.

Nuances of Terms for Divine Creation
The author defines and distinguishes six terms for divine creative acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced meanings of takhliq, insha', fi'l, san', ibda', and tarziq, and how they relate to each other.

Core Idea
Creative terms have similar but distinct meanings centered on bringing into existence.

After establishing the unity of takwin, the author now explores the specific meanings of the various terms used in the Qur'an and hadith for Allah's creative acts. He clarifies that while they share a core meaning, each has a unique shade of meaning that enriches our understanding of divine action.

The final term, tarziq, is defined separately as providing sustenance.

Takwin as an Eternal Attribute and the Created Thing as Temporal
The author proves that takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah and the created thing is temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why takwin (bringing into being) is an eternal attribute of Allah, while the created thing is originated, and how this is analogous to knowledge and power.

Core Idea
The attribute of bringing into existence is eternal; its effect appears in time.

In this passage, the author presents the Ash'ari position on the attribute of takwin. He uses reason and revelation to show that Allah's act of creation is an eternal attribute, but the created thing itself is temporal. The argument hinges on the distinction between an eternal attribute and its temporal relation to creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting key terms like التكوين and المكون. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
This passage is concise, so read it twice.
2
Understand the two proofs
The author gives two proofs: consensus of reason and revelation that Allah is Creator, and the impossibility of applying a derived name without a real attribute.
These proofs establish takwin as an eternal attribute.
3
Study the analogy with knowledge and power
Notice how the author compares takwin to other eternal attributes whose objects are temporal, showing that the eternity of the attribute does not imply eternity of its object.
The term 'relation' (ta'alluq) is key.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Understand the key distinction: the attribute is eternal, but its relation to the creation is originated, so the created thing is temporal.
This avoids the misconception that the world is eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتحقيق أن التكوين صفة أزلية لله تعالى لإطباق العقل والنقل على أنه خالق العالم ومكون له، وامتناع إطلاق اسم المشتق على الشيء من غير أن يكون مأخذ الاشتقاق وصفا له قائما به، فالتكوين ثابت له أزلاً وأبداً والمكوّن حادث بحدوث التعلق كما في العلم والقدرة وغيرهما الصفات القديمة التي لا يلزم من قدمها قدم متعلقاتها لكون تعلقاتها حادثة.
And the verified reality is that takwin (bringing into being) is an eternal attribute of Allah, due to the consensus of reason and revelation that He is the Creator of the world and its Maker, and the impossibility of applying a derived name to a thing without the source of derivation being an attribute subsisting in it. So takwin is established for Him eternally and forever, and the created thing (al-mukawwan) is originated by the origination of the relation, as in knowledge and power and the other eternal attributes, whose eternity does not necessitate the eternity of their objects because their objects are originated.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument proving that takwin (bringing into being) is an eternal attribute of Allah. The author gives two proofs: first, reason and revelation agree that Allah is the Creator and Maker of the world. Second, if we derive the name 'Creator' from takwin, then takwin must be a real attribute subsisting in Allah, otherwise the derivation would be invalid. Therefore, takwin is eternal. However, the created thing (mukawwan) is temporal. He draws an analogy with knowledge and power: these are eternal attributes, but their objects (the known and the powerful) are originated. The eternity of the attribute does not entail the eternity of its object, because the relation (ta'alluq) to the object is originated. This is a standard Ash'ari argument to maintain both the eternity of attributes and the temporality of creation.

Key Terms
التكوين
صفة أزلية
المكون
التعلق
العلم
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since takwin is eternal, the created world must also be eternal.
Correction: The author clarifies that takwin is an eternal attribute, but its object (mukawwan) is temporal. The relation (ta'alluq) is originated, so the created world is not eternal.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that takwin must be an eternal attribute?
A) Because the created world is eternal
B) Because the name 'Creator' is derived from it, and a derived name requires a real basis
C) Because all attributes are eternal
D) Because reason alone proves it

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah, but what it brings into existence is created in time, just as knowledge and power are eternal yet their objects are temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

You are not a surprise to Allah; you were always in His eternal plan. How does this truth change the way you view your purpose and your relationship with Him today? Commit to one specific action that acknowledges that you are the result of His eternal creative will.
?
The passage teaches that the created thing (you and everything around you) is temporal—originated in time. Yet we often live as if this world is permanent. In light of this lesson, what is one attachment you hold that you need to release because it distracts you from the Eternal? Be honest: is there something you fear losing more than you fear losing your connection to Allah? Write down a concrete step to detach from it starting today.
?
When you consider that Allah's attribute of takwin is eternal, but the things He creates are temporal, it means that nothing in this world—no person, no possession, no achievement—can give you lasting security. Only the One with eternal attributes can. Right now, identify one area of your life where you are seeking security from something that will perish. What would it look like to turn that area over to Allah, trusting in His eternal power to provide? Make a firm resolve to do so tonight.

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
The attribute of Takwin is eternal and its object temporal
The author proves that Takwin is eternal and its object temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of Takwin is eternal while its created effect is temporal, based on rational and textual evidence.

Core Idea
The act of making is eternal in Allah; the made thing is not.

This lesson examines the divine attribute of Takwin, the power to bring things into existence. While Allah is described as Creator and Maker, these names imply an eternal attribute of making. However, the objects of that making—the creatures—are temporal. The author provides a careful argument to distinguish between an eternal attribute and its temporal effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a concise, logical style.
2
Identify the two main claims
The passage makes two clear claims: (1) Takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah. (2) The created thing (mukawwan) is temporal. Locate these in the text.
3
Understand the proof
The author gives two proofs: the consensus of reason and revelation, and the linguistic principle that a derived name requires a real attribute. Work through each step.
The linguistic principle is key: if Allah is called 'Maker', the attribute of making must really exist in Him.
4
Examine the analogy
The author compares Takwin to knowledge and power. These attributes are eternal, but their objects (what is known or empowered) are temporal. This illustrates that eternity of attribute does not mean eternity of effect.
This analogy is crucial for avoiding a common misunderstanding.
5
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Many people mistakenly think that if creation is an eternal act, then the world must be eternal. The passage directly addresses this confusion. Make sure you can explain the correct position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتحقيق أن التكوين صفة أزلية لله تعالى لإطباق العقل والنقل على أنه خالق العالم ومكون له، وامتناع إطلاق اسم المشتق على الشيء من غير أن يكون مأخذ الاشتقاق وصفا له قائما به، فالتكوين ثابت له أزلاً وأبداً والمكوّن حادث بحدوث التعلق كما في العلم والقدرة وغيرهما الصفات القديمة التي لا يلزم من قدمها قدم متعلقاتها لكون تعلقاتها حادثة.
And the verification is that Takwin (making/causing to be) is an eternal attribute of Allah Almighty due to the agreement of reason and revelation that He is the Creator of the world and its Maker, and the impossibility of applying a derived name to a thing without the root of derivation being an attribute subsisting in it. So Takwin is established for Him eternally and perpetually, while the created thing (mukawwan) is temporal by the temporality of the relation, just as in knowledge, power, and other eternal attributes whose eternity does not necessitate the eternity of their objects because their objects are temporal.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof concerning the divine attribute of Takwin (making/causing to be). The author affirms that Takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah. He provides two reasons: first, the consensus of reason and revelation that Allah is the Creator and Maker of the world; second, a linguistic principle that a derived name like Khaliq (Creator) or Mukawwin (Maker) cannot be applied to a being unless the root meaning of that derivation—the act of creating or making—exists as an attribute in that being. Since Allah is called Khaliq and Mukawwin, the attribute of Takwin must subsist in Him eternally. The author then clarifies that the attribute itself is eternal, but its object (the mukawwan, the created thing) is temporal, because the relation (ta'alluq) between the attribute and its object is temporal. He compares this to knowledge and power, which are eternal attributes but their objects are temporal. This guards against the misconception that if the attribute is eternal, its effect must also be eternal.

Key Terms
التكوين
صفة أزلية
المكوّن
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the attribute of Takwin is eternal, the world (its object) must also be eternal.
Correction: The attribute is eternal, but its relation to its object (the created thing) is temporal. The object itself is created in time, as seen with knowledge and power: these attributes are eternal, but what is known or empowered comes into being temporally.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between the attribute of Takwin and the created thing (mukawwan)?
A) Both are eternal
B) Takwin is eternal, mukawwan is temporal
C) Takwin is temporal, mukawwan is eternal
D) Both are temporal

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of Allah, but the objects of this attribute—all created things—are temporal, just like the objects of knowledge and power are temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the act of making is eternal in Allah but everything made is temporal, how does that change the way you view the people, possessions, and experiences in your life? Are you clinging to temporary objects as if they are eternal? What would it mean to hold them loosely, knowing they are mere effects of an eternal will?
?
The author uses the analogy of knowledge and power to explain that eternal attributes have temporal objects. Reflect on your own knowledge and power: are they eternal or temporal? How does this contrast humble you before the eternal knowledge and power of Allah? Will you consciously acknowledge His eternal attributes in your daily actions?
?
Do you truly live as if every moment of your existence is sustained by an eternal act of Takwin? Or do you drift into forgetfulness, acting as if you are self-sufficient? What practical step can you take today to remind yourself that you are constantly being 'made' by Allah?

The Eternity of Allah's Names and Attributes and the Past Tense Objection
The author argues for eternal names and attributes and answers the past tense verb objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all of Allah's names and attributes are eternal and how the use of past tense verbs in the Quran does not imply any change in Allah's essence.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal and unchanging; past tense verbs refer to temporal expressions, not His eternal informing.

This passage from the sharh defends a core Sunni doctrine: that Allah's names and attributes are eternal, with no beginning or end. After establishing the proof from Allah's perfection, the author tackles a common objection based on past tense verbs in the Quran. The answer is a fine distinction between the eternal act of informing (al-ikhbar) and the temporal words (al-alfaz) that express it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the two main sections: the statement of the doctrine and its proof, followed by the objection and answer.
The passage uses dense theological language.
2
Understand the proof for eternal attributes
The author argues that since Allah is necessary and perfect, any change would imply imperfection. So all attributes must be eternal.
3
Identify the objection
Look for the sentence that begins 'And here is a famous question...' This is the objection based on past tense Quranic verses.
4
Analyze the answer
The answer distinguishes between the eternal act of informing (ikhbar) and its temporal verbal expressions. The change is only in the words, not in the attribute.
An analogy with knowledge is provided.
5
Connect to overall theology
Reflect on how this answer preserves divine immutability while accounting for temporal language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته لم يحدث له اسم ولا صفة يعني أن صفات الله وأسمائه كلها أزلية لا بداية لها، وأبدية لا نهاية لها، لم يتجدد له تعالى صفة من صفاته ولا اسم من أسمائه، لأنه سبحانه واجب الوجود لذاته، الكامل في ذاته وصفاته، فلو حدث له صفة أو زال عنه نعت لكان قبل حدوث تلك الصفة وبعد زوال ذلك النعت ناقصاً عن مقام الكمال، عن مقام الكمال، وهو في حقه سبحانه المحال من فصفاته تعالى كلها أزلية أبدية، وهاهنا سؤال مشهور وهو أنه قد ورد الإخبار في كلامه سبحانه بلفظ المضي كثيرا نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَا نُوحًا [نوح: ١]، وقال موسى ﴾ [الأعراف:١٠٤] و فَعَلى فِرْعَوْنُ ﴾ [المزمل: ١٦]، والإخبار بلفظ الماضي عما لم يوجد يعد كذباً، والكذب عليه محال. وله جواب مسطور: وهو أن إخباره تعالى لا يتصف أزلاً بالماضي والحال والاستقبال لعدم الزمان، وإنما يتصف بذلك فيما لا يزال بحسب التعلقات فيقال: قام بذات الله تعالى إخبار عن إرسال نوح مطلقاً، وذلك الإخبار موجود أزلاً باق أبداً، فقبل الإرسال كانت العبارة الدالة عليه "إنا نرسل" وبعد الإرسال "إنا أرسلنا" فالتغيير في لفظ الخبر لا في الإخبار القائم بالذات، وهذا كما تقول في علمه تعالى: إنه قائم بذاته سبحانه وتعالى أزلاً العلم بأن نوحاً مرسل وهذا العلم باق أبداً، فقبل وجوده علم أنه سيوجد وبعد وجوده علم بذلك العلم أنه وُجد وأُرسل، والتغيير في المعلوم لا في العلم.
He has never ceased and will never cease with His names and attributes; no name or attribute has occurred for Him. Meaning that all of Allah's attributes and names are eternal with no beginning, and perpetual with no end. No attribute of His attributes nor name of His names has been renewed for Him, because He, glorified, is the Necessary Existent by His essence, perfect in His essence and attributes. So if an attribute occurred for Him or a description ceased from Him, He would have been, before the occurrence of that attribute and after the cessation of that description, deficient from the station of perfection, which is impossible in His case, glorified. So all His attributes are eternal and perpetual. And here is a famous question: namely that reporting in His speech, glorified, with the past tense form occurs frequently, such as His saying: 'Indeed We sent Noah [Nuh: 1]' and 'Moses said' [al-A'raf: 104] and 'And Pharaoh retaliated' [al-Muzzammil: 16]. And reporting with the past tense about what does not exist would be considered a lie, and lying is impossible for Him. And it has a well-known answer: namely that His informing, exalted, is not qualified in eternity by past, present, or future due to the absence of time; rather, it is qualified by that in what will always be according to relations. So it is said: 'In the essence of Allah, Exalted, there subsists an informing about the sending of Noah absolutely, and that informing exists eternally and remains perpetually. So before the sending, the expression indicating it was "We send", and after the sending, "We sent". So the change is in the wording of the report, not in the informing subsisting in the essence. This is like what you say regarding His knowledge, Exalted: It subsists in His essence, glorified, eternally, the knowledge that Noah is sent, and this knowledge remains perpetually. So before his existence, He knew that he would exist, and after his existence, He knew by that knowledge that he existed and was sent. The change is in the known, not in the knowledge.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument for the eternity of Allah's names and attributes, followed by a defense against a common objection. The author first states the doctrine: Allah has never ceased and will never cease with His names and attributes; no name or attribute has occurred for Him anew. He explains that all attributes and names are eternal (azaliyya) and perpetual (abadiyya). The proof: Allah is Necessary Existent (wajib al-wujud) and perfect. If a new attribute occurred or an existing one ceased, He would be imperfect before or after that change, which is impossible. Therefore, all attributes are eternal. The author then raises a famous objection: the Quran frequently uses past tense verbs (e.g., 'We sent Noah'), which would imply that the event occurred before the speech, but if the speech was revealed before the event, it would be a lie—impossible for Allah. The answer: Allah's act of informing (ikhbar) is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not qualified by past/present/future because time does not apply to Him. The change is in the verbal expressions (alfaz) that indicate that eternal informing. Before the event, the expression is future tense; after, it is past tense. The informing itself is unchanging. An analogy is given with Allah's knowledge: He knows eternally that Noah will be sent; that knowledge is unchanging, but the known object (ma'lum) changes from future to past. Thus, the objection is resolved by distinguishing between the eternal attribute and its temporal expressions.

Key Terms
لم يزل ولا يزال
الأسماء والصفات
أزلية أبدية
واجب الوجود
الإخبار
لفظ الماضي
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Past tense verbs in the Quran imply that Allah's speech changes or is false.
Correction: The change is only in the verbal expression, not in the eternal act of informing which is unchanging.

Checkpoint
How does the author resolve the objection that past tense verbs in the Quran would imply change in Allah's speech?
A) He denies that past tense verbs are used in the Quran
B) He says the change is in the verbal expression, not in the eternal informing
C) He says Allah's speech is created and therefore changes
D) He says past tense verbs refer to events that already happened before revelation

Key Takeaway
Allah's names and attributes are eternal and unchanging; the use of past tense verbs in the Quran is a shift in expression, not in Allah's eternal informing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's knowledge of your entire life is eternal and unchanging, do you feel trapped by that knowledge or freed by His eternal grace? How does this truth reshape your daily repentance?
?
When you read the Quran's past tense verses, do you receive them as an eternal address to you now, or as distant history? What would change if you truly believed His words are timeless?
?
The author argues that any change in Allah would imply imperfection. Are you comfortable with your own imperfections in the sight of the Perfect? Or do you secretly wish He would change His judgment about you? How does this teaching force you to depend on His mercy rather than your own deeds?

The Eternity of Allah's Names and Attributes
Explains that Allah's names and attributes are eternal and answers the objection about past tense verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's names and attributes are eternal and how to resolve the apparent contradiction of past tense verses in the Quran.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal; the past tense in the Quran refers to expression, not the attribute itself.

This passage from Imam Abu Hanifa's Fiqh al-Akbar establishes that Allah's names and attributes are eternal—they have no beginning and no end. It then tackles a famous objection: why does the Quran use past tense verbs for events that were future at the time of revelation? The answer clarifies that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, and temporal changes affect only the wording, not the divine speech itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage combines doctrinal statement, proof, objection, and answer.
2
Identify the core claim
The first part states that Allah has never ceased and will never cease to be described with His names and attributes. This is the central thesis.
3
Understand the proof
Why must attributes be eternal? Because Allah is perfect and any new attribute would imply previous deficiency, which is impossible.
This is a key rational argument in kalam.
4
Spot the objection
The objection points to Quranic verses using past tense for events that were future. This seems problematic because using past tense for future events would be false.
5

The answer distinguishes between the eternal attribute of speech (al-ikhbar) and its temporal expression (al-lafz). The change is in the wording, not in the divine attribute.
Analogous to Allah's knowledge: the knowledge is eternal, only the known changes in time.

لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته لم يحدث له اسم ولا صفة فقد ظهر كمال إسلامه وتبين غاية مرامه وأما من استوصف فجهل فليس بمؤمن ولذا قال محمد رحمه الله في 'الجامع الكبير' في صغيرة بين أبوين مسلمين : إذا لم تصف الإسلام حتى أدركت فلم تصف أنها تبين من زوجها». لم يزل ولا يزال بأسمائه وصفاته أي موصوفا بنعوت الكمال ومعروفا بأوصاف الجلال والجمال (لم يحدث له اسم ولا صفة يعني أن صفات الله وأسمائه كلها أزلية لا بداية لها، وأبدية لا نهاية لها، لم يتجدد له تعالى صفة من صفاته ولا اسم من أسمائه، لأنه سبحانه واجب الوجود لذاته، الكامل في ذاته وصفاته، فلو حدث له صفة أو زال عنه نعت لكان قبل حدوث تلك الصفة وبعد زوال ذلك النعت ناقصاً عن مقام الكمال، عن مقام الكمال، وهو في حقه سبحانه المحال من فصفاته تعالى كلها أزلية أبدية، وهاهنا سؤال مشهور وهو أنه قد ورد الإخبار في كلامه سبحانه بلفظ المضي كثيرا نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَا نُوحًا [نوح: ١]، وقال موسى ﴾ [الأعراف:١٠٤] و فَعَلى فِرْعَوْنُ ﴾ [المزمل: ١٦]، والإخبار بلفظ الماضي عما لم يوجد يعد كذباً، والكذب عليه محال. وله جواب مسطور: وهو أن إخباره تعالى لا يتصف أزلاً بالماضي والحال والاستقبال لعدم الزمان، وإنما يتصف بذلك فيما لا يزال بحسب التعلقات فيقال: قام بذات الله تعالى إخبار عن إرسال نوح مطلقاً، وذلك الإخبار موجود أزلاً باق أبداً، فقبل الإرسال كانت العبارة الدالة عليه 'إنا نرسل' وبعد الإرسال 'إنا أرسلنا' فالتغيير في لفظ الخبر لا في الإخبار القائم بالذات، وهذا كما تقول في علمه تعالى: إنه قائم بذاته سبحانه وتعالى أزلاً العلم بأن نوحاً مرسل وهذا العلم باق أبداً، فقبل وجوده علم أنه سيوجد وبعد وجوده علم بذلك العلم أنه وُجد وأُرسل، والتغيير في المعلوم لا في العلم.
He has not ceased and will not cease [to be described] with His names and attributes; no name or attribute has occurred for Him. So the perfection of his Islam has appeared and the utmost of his aim has become clear. As for one who seeks description and is ignorant, he is not a believer. Hence Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said in 'al-Jami' al-Kabir' concerning a minor between two Muslim parents: 'If you do not describe Islam until you have perceived it, then you have not described [it], and she is separated from her husband.' 'He has not ceased and will not cease with His names and attributes' means He is described with attributes of perfection and known with qualities of majesty and beauty. 'No name or attribute has occurred for Him' means that all of Allah's attributes and names are eternal without beginning and everlasting without end; no attribute from His attributes nor name from His names has been renewed for Him, the Exalted, because He, glorified, is necessary of existence in His essence, perfect in His essence and attributes. If an attribute occurred for Him or a description left Him, He would be before the occurrence of that attribute and after the removal of that description deficient from the station of perfection, and that is impossible with respect to Him, the Exalted. So His attributes, the Exalted, are all eternal and everlasting. And here is a famous question: that information has come in His speech, the Exalted, with the past tense form often, such as His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We sent Noah' [Nuh 71:1], and 'Moses said' [al-A'raf 7:104], and 'He drowned Pharaoh' [al-Muzzammil 73:16]. Informing with the past tense about what has not occurred is considered lying, and lying is impossible for Him. And there is a recorded answer: that His informing, the Exalted, is not qualified eternally by past, present, or future because of the absence of time; rather, it is qualified by that [only] in relation to temporal attachments. So it is said: There subsists in the essence of Allah, the Exalted, an information about sending Noah absolutely, and that information exists eternally and remains everlastingly. Before the sending, the expression indicating it was 'We send', and after the sending, 'We sent'. So the change is in the wording of the news, not in the information subsisting in the essence. This is like what you say regarding His knowledge, the Exalted: it subsists in His essence, glorified and exalted, eternally: the knowledge that Noah is sent. And this knowledge remains everlastingly. Before his existence, He knew that he would come into existence; after his existence, He knew by that knowledge that he had come into existence and had been sent. The change is in the known, not in the knowledge.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the eternity of Allah's names and attributes, then addresses a famous objection. The author begins by affirming that Allah has never ceased and will never cease to be described with His names and attributes; no new name or attribute ever occurs for Him. This statement is clarified: Allah is eternally described with perfect and majestic attributes. The reason is that Allah is necessary of existence, perfect in essence and attributes. If any attribute were to begin or cease, He would be temporarily deficient—impossible for Him. Thus all attributes are eternal and everlasting. Next, the author presents a famous objection: The Quran uses past tense verbs (e.g., 'We sent Noah') even though the events were future at the time of revelation. Using past tense for future events would be false, but falsehood from Allah is impossible. The answer is that Allah's act of informing (al-ikhbar) is not temporally qualified because time does not apply to Him. Rather, the information (al-ikhbar) subsists in His essence as an eternal truth. The change is only in the wording that expresses that information relative to the time of the event. Before the event, the wording is future; after, it is past. This is analogous to Allah's knowledge: His knowledge of an event is eternal and unchanging; only the known object changes in time. Thus the objection is resolved by distinguishing between the eternal divine speech and its temporal expression.

Misconception: The past tense in the Quran implies that Allah's speech is temporal or that His attributes change over time.
Correction: The past tense refers to the expression of the eternal attribute of speech, not to the attribute itself. The divine speech is timeless and unchanging.

The Five Eternal Attributes of Allah
Lists five essential attributes of Allah and explains their eternity and distinction from created things

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five essential attributes of Allah enumerated by Imam Abu Hanifa and why each is eternal and uncreated, while their effects are created in time.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal, uncreated, and distinct from their temporal created effects.

Imam Abu Hanifa, in his Fiqh al-Akbar, lists five fundamental attributes belonging to Allah's essence. These are not acquired or temporal; they are eternal and inseparable from who He is. This passage establishes that while the attributes are eternal, the objects of these attributes—such as created things—are brought into existence in time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the repeated structure: 'lam yazal ... bi ...' and the affirmation that each attribute is eternal (ṣifah fī al-azal).
The passage uses a pattern to emphasize the eternity of each attribute.
2
Identify the five attributes
As you read, list the five attributes: Knowledge (ʿilm), Power (qudra), Speech (kalām), Creating (takhlīq), and Action (fiʿl). Observe that each is described as an attribute in eternity (ṣifah fī al-azal).
These are the essential attributes according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the key distinction
Note the contrast: attributes like knowledge and power are eternal and uncreated, whereas the 'object of action' (mafʿūl) is created (makhlooq). This distinction is crucial to avoid confusing the Creator with creation.
The text explicitly states: 'al-mafʿūl makhlooq wa fiʿl Allāh ghayr makhlooq.'
4
Reflect on the argument against creation of attributes
The commentary mentions that if Allah's action were created, it would require multiple creators. Reflect on why this is logically impossible in Islamic theology.
This argument prevents an infinite regress of creators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفات الله أزلية لم يزل عالماً بعلمه والعلم صفة في الأزل، وقادراً بقدرته والقدرة صفة في الأزل، ومتكلماً بكلامه والكلام صفةٌ في الأزل، وخالقاً بتخليقه والتخليق صفة في الأزل، وفاعلاً بفعله والفعل صفةٌ في الأزل، والفاعل هو الله تعالى والفعل صفة في الأزل، والمفعول مخلوق وفعل الله تعالى غير مخلوق (لم يزل عالماً بعلمه أي بعلمه الذي هو صفته الأزلية لا بعلم لاحق يلزم منه جهل سابق، وهذا معنى قوله (والعلم صفةٌ في الأزل يعني وما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه، فعلمه أزلي أبدي منزه عن قبول الزيادة والنقصان، بخلاف علوم أرباب العرفان. (وقادراً بقدرته) صفته الأزلية لا بقدرة حادثة في الأمور الكونية والقدرة صفةٌ في الأزل) أي بقدرته التي هي وكذا نعته في المستقبل ومتكلماً بكلامه أي الذاتي القدسي (والكلام) أي النفسي (صفةٌ في الأزل، وخالقاً بتخليقه والتخليق صفةٌ في الأزل، وفاعلاً بفعله والفعل) أي وفعله كما في نسخة (صفة في الأزل يعني إذا خلق شيئا ابتداء وفعله فعلا انتهاء، فإنما يخلقه ويفعله بفعله الذي هو صفته الأزلية، لا بفعل حادث ووصف حادث عند خلقه وفعله، إذ لا يحدث له علم ولا قدرة ولا خلق ولا فعل بحدوث المعلوم والمقدور والمخلوق والمفعول وهذا معنى قوله: (والفاعل هو الله تعالى أي لا شريك له في وصنعه وحكمه وأمره (والفعل) أي وفعله كما في نسخة (صفةٌ في الأزل والمفعول مخلوق) أي حادث عند تعلق فعله سبحانه به وفعل الله تعالى غیر مخلوق أي ليس بحادث بل هو قديم كفاعله، إذ لا يلزم من كون المفعول مخلوقاً كون الفعل مخلوقاً، وفي كلام الإمام الأعظم إيماء إلى أنه لو كان فعل الله مخلوقاً لزم تعدد الخالق وقد ثبت أن الله سبحانه خالق كل شيء، فله سبحانه
The attributes of Allah are eternal. He has not ceased to be knowing by His knowledge, and knowledge is an attribute in eternity; and powerful by His power, and power is an attribute in eternity; and speaking by His speech, and speech is an attribute in eternity; and creating by His act of creating, and the act of creating is an attribute in eternity; and acting by His action, and the action is an attribute in eternity. The Agent is Allah, the Exalted, and the action is an attribute in eternity, and the object of action is created, and the action of Allah, the Exalted, is not created. 'He has not ceased to be knowing by His knowledge' means by His knowledge which is His eternal attribute, not by a later knowledge that would entail previous ignorance. This is the meaning of His saying: 'and knowledge is an attribute in eternity'—that is, whatever is proven to be pre-eternal, its non-existence is impossible. So His knowledge is eternal and everlasting, free from accepting increase or decrease, unlike the knowledges of the masters of gnosis. 'And powerful by His power'—His eternal attribute, not by a temporal power in cosmic matters; and power is an attribute in eternity. That is, by His power which is [eternal], and similarly His description in the future. 'And speaking by His speech'—the essential, holy speech; 'and speech'—the internal speech—'is an attribute in eternity. 'And creating by His act of creating, and the act of creating is an attribute in eternity. 'And acting by His action, and the action'—that is, His action, as in one copy—'is an attribute in eternity.' That is, when He creates something initially and does something finally, He creates it and does it by His action which is His eternal attribute, not by a temporal action and temporal description at the time of His creating and doing. For no knowledge, power, creation, or action occurs for Him due to the occurrence of the known, the empowered, the created, and the acted-upon. This is the meaning of His saying: 'And the Agent is Allah, the Exalted'—that is, no partner for Him in His making, judgment, and command. 'And the action'—that is, His action, as in one copy—'is an attribute in eternity; and the object of action is created'—that is, temporal at the time of the attachment of His action, the Exalted, to it. And the action of Allah, the Exalted, is not created—that is, it is not temporal, rather it is eternal like its Agent. For it does not follow from the object of action being created that the action is created. And in the speech of the Greatest Imam there is an indication that if the act of Allah were created, multiple creators would be necessary, and it has been established that Allah, the Exalted, is the Creator of everything. So for Him, the Exalted...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage enumerates five essential attributes of Allah—knowledge, power, speech, creating, and action—and establishes that each is an eternal attribute of His essence. The author explains that Allah has never ceased to be knowing by His knowledge, which is eternal, not acquired; otherwise prior ignorance would be implied. Similarly, His power is eternal, not temporal. His speech is the internal, essential speech, eternal. His act of creating (takhlīq) and His action (fi'l) are attributes in eternity. The key distinction is between the eternal attribute and its temporal object: the attribute (e.g., creation) is eternal, while the created thing (maf'ūl) is temporal. The action of Allah is not created, otherwise it would imply a regress of creators or multiple creators. The passage concludes by noting that the Imam Abu Hanifa implied that if Allah's action were created, it would necessitate multiple creators, which contradicts that Allah is the Creator of everything. Thus, the attributes are eternal and uncreated, while their effects are created in time.

Correction: The attributes are eternal; only the objects of these attributes (the created things) are temporal. The attributes themselves are uncreated and unchanging.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's knowledge is eternal and never increases or changes, why do you still worry that your hidden struggles might be unknown to Him? How would your daily secret thoughts change if you truly believed His knowledge covers every detail of your life?
?
Since Allah's action is uncreated and does not depend on anything, in what areas of your life are you still acting as if your own efforts create results independently? What would it mean for you to let go of that illusion today?
?
If Allah's power is eternal and not acquired, then your own limited power is borrowed moment by moment. What is one thing you are clinging to that you really have no power over, and how can you surrender it to the One whose power never fades?

The Eternity of God's Attributes and the Act-Object Distinction
Enumeration of five eternal divine attributes and the act-object distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all of God's attributes are eternal and how His eternal act differs from the created object.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal; His act is uncreated, but its object is created.

This passage from the Fiqh al-Akbar establishes a foundational principle of Sunni theology: that God's attributes—knowledge, power, speech, creative act, and act—are eternal, not acquired at the moment of creation. It also clarifies a subtle distinction between God's act (fi'l) and the object of that act (maf'ul), affirming that the act is uncreated while the object is created. Understanding this distinction helps prevent misconceptions about God's relationship with creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the complete Arabic text once, then its literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
Notice the repetition of 'صفة في الأزل' for each attribute.
2
Identify the five attributes
List the five attributes mentioned: knowledge, power, speech, creative act, and act. Observe that each is described as an eternal attribute.
3
Focus on the act-object distinction
Pay attention to the last part where the text distinguishes between God's act (fi'l) and its object (maf'ul). Note that the act is eternal and uncreated, while the object is created.
This is a key theological point.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the text emphasizes that the act is not created. The commentary explains that if the act were created, it would imply multiple creators.
This rejects any notion of created attributes.

لم يزل عالماً بعلمه والعلم صفة في الأزل، وقادراً بقدرته والقدرة صفة في الأزل، ومتكلماً بكلامه والكلام صفةٌ في الأزل، وخالقاً بتخليقه والتخليق صفة في الأزل، وفاعلاً بفعله والفعل صفةٌ في الأزل، والفاعل هو الله تعالى والفعل صفة في الأزل، والمفعول مخلوق وفعل الله تعالى غير مخلوق (لم يزل عالماً بعلمه أي بعلمه الذي هو صفته الأزلية لا بعلم لاحق يلزم منه جهل سابق، وهذا معنى قوله (والعلم صفةٌ في الأزل يعني وما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه، فعلمه أزلي أبدي منزه عن قبول الزيادة والنقصان، بخلاف علوم أرباب العرفان. (وقادراً بقدرته) صفته الأزلية لا بقدرة حادثة في الأمور الكونية والقدرة صفةٌ في الأزل) محمد أي بقدرته التي هي وكذا نعته في المستقبل ومتكلماً بكلامه أي الذاتي القدسي (والكلام) أي النفسي (صفةٌ في الأزل، وخالقاً بتخليقه والتخليق صفةٌ في الأزل، وفاعلاً بفعله والفعل) أي وفعله كما في نسخة (صفة في الأزل يعني إذا خلق شيئا ابتداء وفعله فعلا انتهاء، فإنما يخلقه ويفعله بفعله الذي هو صفته الأزلية، لا بفعل حادث ووصف حادث عند خلقه وفعله، إذ لا يحدث له علم ولا قدرة ولا خلق ولا فعل بحدوث المعلوم والمقدور والمخلوق والمفعول وهذا معنى قوله: (والفاعل هو الله تعالى أي لا شريك له في وصنعه وحكمه وأمره (والفعل) أي وفعله كما في نسخة (صفةٌ في الأزل والمفعول مخلوق) أي حادث عند تعلق فعله سبحانه به وفعل الله تعالى غیر مخلوق أي ليس بحادث بل هو قديم كفاعله، إذ لا يلزم من كون المفعول مخلوقاً كون الفعل مخلوقاً، وفي كلام الإمام الأعظم إيماء إلى أنه لو كان فعل الله مخلوقاً لزم تعدد الخالق وقد ثبت أن الله سبحانه خالق كل شيء، فله سبحانه
He has never ceased to be knowing by His knowledge, and knowledge is an attribute in pre-eternity; and powerful by His power, and power is an attribute in pre-eternity; and speaking by His speech, and speech is an attribute in pre-eternity; and creator by His act of creating, and the act of creating is an attribute in pre-eternity; and agent by His act, and the act is an attribute in pre-eternity; and the agent is Allah Most High, and the act is an attribute in pre-eternity; and the object is created, and the act of Allah Most High is not created. (He has never ceased to be knowing by His knowledge, i.e., by His knowledge which is His eternal attribute, not by a subsequent knowledge that would necessitate prior ignorance; and this is the meaning of his saying: 'and knowledge is an attribute in pre-eternity,' meaning, whatever is established as pre-eternal, its non-existence is impossible. So His knowledge is eternal and everlasting, free from increase or decrease, unlike the knowledges of the people of spiritual insight. (And powerful by His power), His eternal attribute, not by a contingent power in cosmic matters; and power is an attribute in pre-eternity.) Muhammad—i.e., by His power which is, and likewise His description in the future. And speaking by His speech, i.e., the essential, holy speech; (and speech), i.e., the internal speech, (is an attribute in pre-eternity). And creator by His act of creating, and the act of creating is an attribute in pre-eternity; and agent by His act, and the act (i.e., as in one copy: 'and His act') is an attribute in pre-eternity, meaning: when He creates something initially and brings it into existence finally, He only creates it and brings it into existence by His act which is His eternal attribute, not by a contingent act and a contingent attribute at the time of His creating and bringing into existence. For there arises for Him no knowledge, no power, no creation, no act with the occurrence of the known, the empowered, the created, and the effected. And this is the meaning of His saying: (And the agent is Allah Most High, i.e., no partner to Him in His making, His judgment, and His command. (And the act), i.e., as in one copy: 'and His act' (is an attribute in pre-eternity; and the object is created), i.e., contingent upon the attachment of His act to it, and the act of Allah Most High is not created, i.e., not contingent, but rather eternal like its agent. For it does not follow from the object being created that the act is created. And in the saying of the Great Imam there is an indication that if the act of Allah were created, it would necessitate a multiplicity of creators, and it has been established that Allah Most High is the Creator of everything, so to Him belongs...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the eternity of God's attributes and the distinction between God's act (fi'l) and the object of that act (maf'ul). It begins by stating that God has never ceased to be knowing, powerful, speaking, creating, and acting by His eternal attributes—knowledge, power, speech, creative act, and act—each of which is an attribute in pre-eternity (azal). The commentary then elaborates on each phrase: 'knowing by His knowledge' means His knowledge is an eternal attribute, not a later acquisition that would imply prior ignorance; what is pre-eternal cannot cease. Similarly, 'powerful by His power' means His power is eternal, not contingent. 'Speaking by His speech' refers to the essential, internal speech (kalam nafsi), which is eternal. 'Creator by His act of creating' and 'agent by His act' mean that when He creates or acts, He does so by His eternal attribute of creation and act, not by a new, contingent attribute; He does not acquire knowledge, power, creation, or act at the moment of creation. The passage then clarifies that the agent is Allah alone, without partner, and that His act is eternal, while the object (the created thing) is contingent, occurring when His eternal act attaches to it. It emphatically denies that the act could be created, as that would imply multiple creators. The author notes that this is an indication from the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa) that if God's act were created, it would necessitate a second creator, contradicting the fact that Allah is the Creator of all things.
