The Ash'ari View on Takwin and Divine Acts
Presents and evaluates the Ash'ari view on takwin with Hanafi support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that takwin is identical to power and how it is supported by Hanafi sources, particularly the statement of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Takwin is power at work — no separate attribute needed.

This passage presents a key debate in Islamic theology: is the attribute of bringing into existence (takwin) distinct from divine power, or is it simply power in relation to its objects? The Ash'ari school argues the latter, and the commentator Ibn al-Humam shows that even Hanafi sources, including Abu Hanifa himself, support this view. Let us examine the arguments closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari claim
Start by reading the first part of the passage where the Ash'ari position is stated. Notice how they define takwin as power with a specific attachment.
Take note of the terms 'takhliq' and 'tarziq' as examples.
2
Understand the concept of attachment (ta'alluq)
The Ash'aris say the attributes of acts are contingent because they are attachments of power. Reflect on why attachments are considered contingent.
This is a key point in their argument.
3
Examine Ibn al-Humam's response
Read Ibn al-Humam's comment where he argues that the Hanafi view on takwin does not contradict the Ash'ari position. Identify how he uses Abu Hanifa's words.
Look for the phrase 'ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير'.
4
Analyze the quote from Abu Hanifa
Carefully read the quote from al-Tahawi. Notice how it emphasizes that Allah's names like 'Creator' are eternal based on His power.
The commentator explains that this quote supports the Ash'ari view.
5
Reflect on the methodological principle
The passage ends by warning that implied meanings (mafhum) should not contradict explicit texts (mantuq). Think about how this principle applies to the discussion.
This is a minor but important point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا، والأشاعرة يقولون: ليست صفة التكوين سوى صفة القدرة بإعتبار تعلقها بمتعلق خاص، فالتخليق هو القدرة بإعتبار تعلقها بالمخلوق، وكذا الترزيق ويقولون: صفات الأفعال حادثة؛ لأنها عبارة عن تعلقات القدرة والتعلقات حادثة. قال ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى : وما ذكره مشايخ الحنفية في معنى التكوين من أنها صفات تدل على تأثير لا ينفي قول الأشاعرة ولا يوجب كون صفة التكوين على فصولها صفات أخرى لا ترجع إلى القدرة المتعلقة والإرادة المتعلقة بل في كلام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ما يفيد أن ذلك على ما فهم الأشاعرة من هذه الصفات على ما نقله الطحاوي عنه حيث قال: وكما كان الله تعالى بصفاته أزلياً كذلك لا يزال عليها أبدياً، ليس منذ خلق الخلق استفاد اسم الخالق ولا بإحداثه البرية استفاد اسم الباري، بل له معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب ومعنى الخالقية ولا مخلوق، كما أنه . ـه محيي الموتى استحق هذا الاسم قبل إحيائهم، كذلك استحق اسم الخالق قبل إنشائهم، ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير. انتهى. فقوله ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير تعليل وبيان لاستحقاق اسم الخالق قبل المخلوق، فأفاد أن معنی الخالق قبل الخلق واستحقاق اسم الخالق بسبب قيام قدرته تعالى على الخلق، فاسم الخالق أزلي ولا مخلوق في الأزل لمن له قدرة الخلق في الأزل، وهذا ما يقوله الأشاعرة. انتهى. وفيه أن المفهوم لا يعارض المنطوق المعلوم.
Now, the Ash'aris say: The attribute of bringing into existence (takwin) is nothing other than the attribute of power (qudra) with consideration of its attachment to a specific object. So creating (takhliq) is power with consideration of its attachment to the created, and similarly providing (tarziq). And they say: The attributes of acts (sifat al-af'al) are contingent (haditha), because they are expressions of attachments of power, and attachments are contingent. Ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, said: What the Hanafi masters mentioned concerning the meaning of takwin—that they are attributes indicating effect—does not negate the Ash'ari statement nor necessitate that the attribute of takwin in its details are other attributes not reducible to attached power and attached will. Rather, in the statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, there is something indicating that this is as the Ash'aris understood these attributes, according to what al-Tahawi transmitted from him, where he said: 'Just as Allah Most High was eternal with His attributes, so too He will remain upon them eternally. He did not acquire the name 'Creator' from the time He created creation, nor did He acquire the name 'Maker' by bringing about creatures. Rather, He has the meaning of Lordship without a lord, and the meaning of Creatorhood without a created being. Just as He—[?]—the Reviver of the dead deserved this name before reviving them, so too He deserved the name 'Creator' before creating them. That is because He is over all things powerful.' End. So his saying 'that is because He is over all things powerful' is an explanation and clarification of the deserving of the name 'Creator' before the created. It indicates that the meaning of 'Creator' before creation and the deserving of the name 'Creator' are due to the establishment of His power over creation. So the name 'Creator' is eternal, and there is no created being in pre-eternity for one who has the power of creation in pre-eternity. And this is what the Ash'aris say. End. And in it, (there is the point that) the implied meaning does not contradict the explicit text.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents and evaluates the Ash'ari position on the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) and the nature of divine acts. It begins by stating the Ash'ari view: the attribute of takwin is not distinct from power (qudra) but is power considered with a specific attachment (ta'alluq) to its object. For example, 'creating' (takhliq) is simply power attached to the created thing, and similarly 'providing' (tarziq) is power attached to provision. The Ash'aris further assert that the 'attributes of acts' (sifat al-af'al)—like creating, providing, etc.—are contingent (haditha) because they consist of the attachments of power, and attachments are contingent events. The commentator then cites Ibn al-Humam's response: the Hanafi characterization of takwin as attributes indicating effect does not refute the Ash'ari view nor require that these attributes be entirely separate from attached power and will. In fact, Ibn al-Humam claims that Abu Hanifa's own statements, as transmitted by al-Tahawi, support the Ash'ari understanding. The Tahawi quote emphasizes that Allah's names like 'Creator' are eternal and not acquired at the moment of creation; He deserved the name 'Creator' before any creation because He is 'over all things powerful.' The commentator explains that this justification ties the name 'Creator' to God's eternal power over creation, thus affirming that the name is eternal even without a created object. This, he concludes, is exactly what the Ash'aris hold. The passage ends with a cautionary note: implied understandings (mafhum) should not contradict explicit textual statements (mantuq). This suggests a methodological principle for interpreting the sources.

Checkpoint

A) A separate eternal attribute distinct from power.
B) Power considered with a particular attachment.
C) A contingent attribute that arises with creation.
D) The act of the power that is itself created.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari view that takwin is power with attachment is supported by Abu Hanifa's statement that God deserved the name Creator before creation because of His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that God's name 'Creator' is eternal because He has the power to create, even before any creation existed. Does your heart truly believe that God was always worthy of that name, or do you subtly tie His worthiness to His actions? This week, practice praising God as 'al-Khaliq' during your prayers, consciously affirming His eternal perfection independent of creation.
?
The passage warns against letting implied meanings contradict explicit texts. Think of an area in your faith where your reasoning tempts you to prioritize your own understanding over clear revelation. What explicit verse or hadith are you tempted to reinterpret? Commit to submitting to the apparent meaning (zahir) until it is properly reconciled by qualified scholars.
?
The Ash'aris affirm that God's power is enough for all acts, without needing separate attributes. Do you truly trust that God's power is sufficient for every situation in your life, or do you doubt when your prayers seem unanswered? This week, whenever you feel anxious, remind yourself: 'He is over all things powerful' and write down one specific fear to entrust to His power.

The Attribute of Takwin: Hanafi-Ash'ari Debate
The author presents the Hanafi-Ash'ari debate on takwin and Ibn al-Humann's reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing Hanafi and Ash'ari views on the attribute of takwin and Ibn al-Humann's argument that they can be reconciled.

Core Idea
Takwin is either a distinct eternal attribute or merely a relation of power.

This passage delves into a classic theological debate about the nature of the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The Ash'aris argue that takwin is not separate from divine power but merely a relation, while the Hanafis maintain it is a distinct eternal attribute. Ibn al-Humann enters the discussion, attempting to reconcile the two positions by citing a statement from Abu Hanifa himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage carefully to pinpoint the Ash'ari and Hanafi views on takwin. Notice how each side defines the attribute in relation to power (qudra).
The Ash'ari view reduces takwin to a relation of power; the Hanafi view treats it as an independent attribute.
2
Follow Ibn al-Humann's argument
Ibn al-Humann challenges the Hanafi masters and then appeals to Abu Hanifa's words to show that the Hanafi position does not contradict the Ash'ari view. Trace his logic.
He uses al-Tahawi's transmission to argue that Abu Hanifa's understanding aligns with the Ash'aris.
3
Analyze the concluding remark
The passage ends with a statement that the understood meaning does not contradict the explicit wording. Reflect on what this implies about the relationship between the two schools.
4
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you grasp the Ash'ari definition of takwin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأغرب ابن الهمام حيث ذهل عن هذا الكلام فقال: وليس في كلام أبي حنيفة تصريح بأن صفة التكوين قديمة زائدة على الصفات المتقدمة ما أخذه سوی المتأخرون من قوله : كان الله تعالى خالقا قبل أن يخلق ورازقا قبل أن يرزق. هذا، والأشاعرة يقولون: ليست صفة التكوين سوى صفة القدرة بإعتبار تعلقها بمتعلق خاص، فالتخليق هو القدرة بإعتبار تعلقها بالمخلوق، وكذا الترزيق ويقولون: صفات الأفعال حادثة؛ لأنها عبارة عن تعلقات القدرة والتعلقات حادثة. قال ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى : وما ذكره مشايخ الحنفية في معنى التكوين من أنها صفات تدل على تأثير لا ينفي قول الأشاعرة ولا يوجب كون صفة التكوين على فصولها صفات أخرى لا ترجع إلى القدرة المتعلقة والإرادة المتعلقة بل في كلام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ما يفيد أن ذلك على ما فهم الأشاعرة من هذه الصفات على ما نقله الطحاوي عنه حيث قال: وكما كان الله تعالى بصفاته أزلياً كذلك لا يزال عليها أبدياً، ليس منذ خلق الخلق استفاد اسم الخالق ولا بإحداثه البرية استفاد اسم الباري، بل له معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب ومعنى الخالقية ولا مخلوق، كما أنه محيي الموتى استحق هذا الاسم قبل إحيائهم، كذلك استحق اسم الخالق قبل إنشائهم، ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير. انتهى. فقوله ذلك بأنه على كل شيء قدير تعليل وبيان لاستحقاق اسم الخالق قبل المخلوق، فأفاد أن معنى الخالق قبل الخلق واستحقاق اسم الخالق بسبب قيام قدرته تعالى على الخلق، فاسم الخالق أزلي ولا مخلوق في الأزل لمن له قدرة الخلق في الأزل، وهذا ما يقوله الأشاعرة. انتهى. وفيه أن المفهوم لا يعارض المنطوق المعلوم.
And Ibn al-Humann was stranger, having been heedless of this statement, and he said: There is not in the speech of Abu Hanifa an explicit statement that the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) is eternal and additional to the preceding attributes, except what the later scholars took from his saying: 'Allah was Creator before He created, and Provider before He provided.' This, and the Ash'aris say: The attribute of takwin is nothing other than the attribute of power (qudra) in consideration of its relation to a specific object, so bringing into existence (takhlīq) is power in consideration of its relation to the created, and similarly providing (tarzīq). And they say: The attributes of actions are contingent because they are expressions of the relations of power, and relations are contingent. Ibn al-Humann, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And what the Hanafi masters mentioned regarding the meaning of takwin – that they are attributes indicating influence – does not negate the Ash'ari statement nor necessitate that the attribute of takwin in its aspects is another attribute not reducible to related power and related will. Rather, in the speech of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, there is that which indicates that this is according to what the Ash'aris understood of these attributes, as al-Tahawi reported from him where he said: 'Just as Allah was eternal with His attributes, likewise He will never cease to be upon them eternally. It is not that since He created creation He acquired the name Creator, nor by His bringing about creatures did He acquire the name Maker. Rather, He has the meaning of lordship without any lord, and the meaning of Creatorship without any created, just as He is the Reviver of the dead – He deserved this name before reviving them; likewise He deserved the name Creator before creating them. That is because He is over all things capable.' End. So his saying 'That is because He is over all things capable' is a cause and explanation for deserving the name Creator before the created. So it indicated that the meaning of Creator before creation and deserving the name Creator is due to the establishment of His power over creation. So the name Creator is eternal and there is no created thing in eternity for one who has the power to create in eternity, and this is what the Ash'aris say. End. And in it [there is] that the understood meaning does not contradict the explicit wording.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the nature of the divine attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). It presents the Hanafi-Ash'ari debate. The author first notes Ibn al-Humann's objection that Abu Hanifa never explicitly said takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from others; rather, later scholars inferred it from statements like 'He was Creator before creating.' Then the Ash'ari position is summarized: takwin is not a separate attribute but merely qudra (power) considered in relation to a specific object. Attributes of actions (like creating and providing) are deemed contingent because they are relations, and relations are temporally contingent. Ibn al-Humann then argues that the Hanafi masters' description of takwin as 'attributes indicating influence' does not conflict with the Ash'ari view and does not make takwin a separate set of attributes unrelated to related power and will. He appeals to a statement by Abu Hanifa transmitted by al-Tahawi: Allah's names 'Creator' and 'Maker' are eternal because His power over creation is eternal, not because creation exists eternally. The passage concludes that this understanding matches the Ash'ari position, and that the implicit meaning (taken from Abu Hanifa's words) does not contradict the explicit wording of the Hanafi masters.

ابن الهمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hanafi and Ash'ari positions on takwin are irreconcilable and contradict each other.
Correction: Ibn al-Humann shows that the Hanafi masters' view of takwin as influencing attributes does not negate the Ash'ari position, and that Abu Hanifa's own words align with the Ash'ari understanding of eternal names based on eternal power.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view presented in this passage, what is the attribute of takwin?
A) A separate eternal attribute distinct from qudra
B) Merely qudra (power) considered in relation to its specific object
C) An attribute that is conditional upon the existence of creatures
D) The same as the attribute of will (irada)

Key Takeaway
The debate over takwin hinges on whether it is a distinct eternal attribute or a relational aspect of power, and Ibn al-Humann argues that the two positions can be reconciled by understanding Abu Hanifa's own statements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological position that is different from what you were taught, do you honestly examine the source texts to see if there is common ground, or do you immediately dismiss it as false? Are you willing to be like Ibn al-Humann, who found reconciliation where others saw only conflict?
?
Reflect on a time in your own life when you were certain that someone else’s view was wrong, only to later realize that both sides had a valid perspective. How did that shift affect your relationship with that person and your humility before God? This lesson reminds us that even great scholars can be heedless—could you be blinded by sectarian loyalty?
?
If God’s attributes are eternal and His names like 'Creator' are meaningful even without a creation, what does that mean for your daily reliance on Him? Do you only turn to Him as Creator when you need something, or do you recognize that His power and care for you are constant, even when you are unaware?

Divine Attributes

Allah's Attributes Are Eternal and Uncreated
Affirmation of eternal attributes and ruling on denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes are eternal and uncreated, and that denying or doubting them regarding the well-known attributes constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal; denying or doubting them is disbelief.

This passage from the Sharh establishes a foundational point in Islamic theology: the attributes of Allah are not created, but are eternal in pre-eternity. It then issues a strong ruling that anyone who claims they are created, halts judgment, or doubts them falls into disbelief. The passage also clarifies which specific attributes are at stake, so that the ruling is precise and not overextended.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the overall argument. Notice the strong opening statement.
The passage combines affirmation with a conditional ruling.
2
Identify the three positions that lead to disbelief
Note the three conditions: saying attributes are created, halting (waqf), or doubting (shakk). Understand what each means from the commentary.
Halting means refusing to decide whether they are eternal or temporal.
3
Learn the list of attributes
The passage ends by specifying the attributes for which ignorance or doubt causes disbelief. Memorize these nine attributes: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, takhlīq, and tarzīq.
These are the well-known attributes mentioned in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفاته في الأزل غير محدثة ولا مخلوقة فمن قال إنها مخلوقة أو محدثة أو وقف أو شك فيها فهو كافر بالله تعالى. هو تأكيد وتأييد أي غير محدثة بإحداثه ولا مخلوقة بخلق غيره. فمن قال إنها مخلوقة أو محدثة أو وقف) أي بأن لا يحكم بأنها قديمة أو حادثة ويؤخر طلب معرفتها ولا يقول آمنت بالله وصفاته على وفق مراده أو شك فيها) أي تردد في هذه المسألة ونحوها سواء يستوي طرفاه أو يترجح ونحوها سواء يستوي طرفاه أو يترجح أحدهما فهو كافر بالله تعالى أي ببعض صفاته وهو مكلف بأن يكون عارفاً بذاته وجميع صفاته، إلا أن الجهل والشك أعني الموجبين للكفر مخصوصان بصفات الله المذكورة من النعوت المسطورة المشهورة، الحياة والقدرة والعلم والكلام والسمع والبصر والإرادة والتخليق والترزيق.
And His attributes are not originated nor created in eternity. So whoever says they are created or originated, or halts, or doubts concerning them, is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty. It is an affirmation and confirmation, i.e., not originated by His origination nor created by creation of another. So whoever says they are created or originated, or halts – i.e., by not ruling that they are eternal or temporal and delays seeking knowledge of them and does not say 'I believe in Allah and His attributes according to His will' – or doubts them – i.e., wavers in this matter and its like, whether the two sides are equal or one outweighs, and its like whether the two sides are equal or one outweighs – then he is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty, i.e., in some of His attributes. And he is obligated to know His essence and all His attributes, except that ignorance and doubt – I mean the two causes of disbelief – are particular to the mentioned attributes of Allah from the well-known traits recorded and famous: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, bringing into existence (takhlīq), and providing (tarzīq).
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and ruling (hukm) regarding the eternity of God's attributes. It begins by declaring that God's attributes in pre-eternity (al-azal) are neither originated (muhdatha) nor created (makhluqa). Then it states the severe consequence: anyone who says they are created or originated, or suspends judgment (waqf), or doubts, is a disbeliever in Allah. The author provides a commentary: this is a confirmation that the attributes are not originated by God's own act of origination nor created by another's creation. The conditional clauses are unpacked: 'halting' (waqf) means refusing to rule whether the attributes are eternal or temporal and deferring knowledge; 'doubt' (shakk) means hesitation. Both lead to disbelief. However, the author clarifies that this disbelief is in some of God's attributes, and everyone is obligated to know God's essence and all attributes. Yet the ignorance and doubt that necessitate disbelief are restricted to the well-known attributes listed: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, takhlīq, and tarzīq. This enumeration specifies which attributes are absolutely necessary to affirm as uncreated.

محدثة

شك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any doubt about any attribute of Allah constitutes disbelief.
Correction: The passage clarifies that this ruling applies only to the well-known attributes listed (life, power, knowledge, etc.), not to every attribute.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is NOT among the attributes ignorance or doubt of which causes disbelief?
A) Life (al-hayat)
B) Power (al-qudra)
C) Eternity in the future (al-baqa')
D) Hearing (al-sam')

Key Takeaway
Affirming the uncreated nature of Allah's attributes is essential to faith; denying or doubting them regarding the nine well-known attributes is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever internally hesitated or felt uncertain about any of Allah's attributes, perhaps thinking 'it doesn't matter'? The passage equates that hesitation to disbelief. Will you now consciously affirm all nine attributes without reservation?
?
Do you take the names and attributes of Allah lightly in your speech or thoughts, not realizing the gravity of denying them? Commit to memorizing these nine attributes and safeguarding your tongue and heart from any doubt about them.
?
If someone asked you today, 'Are Allah's attributes created or eternal?' would you answer with absolute certainty? Halting or delaying your answer is itself disbelief according to this passage. Can you say with conviction, 'I believe in Allah and His attributes as He wills'?

The Quran as Uncreated Speech
Author distinguishes the eternal Quran from its temporal forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran is Allah's eternal attribute of speech, and that its written, recited, and preserved forms are not themselves the eternal speech.

Core Idea
The Quran's eternal meaning is uncreated; its written and recited forms are temporal.

This passage distinguishes between the Quran as the eternal speech of Allah and its physical manifestations in writing, recitation, and memory. It also warns against denying this distinction. Read carefully to grasp this foundational Ash'ari doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its rhythm and key terms. Notice the repeated pattern: 'maktub, mahfuz, maqru'.
2
Identify the three modes
The passage says the Quran is written in mus'hafs, preserved in hearts, and recited on tongues. Recognize that these are physical, created forms.
3
Understand the distinction
The passage ends with 'al-maqru' qadim wa-al-qira'a haditha' — the recited (the Quran itself) is eternal, the recitation (the human act) is temporal. This is the key insight.
4
Reflect on the warning
The passage warns that denying the eternity of Allah's speech leads to disbelief. This shows the high stakes of this doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في القرآن. والقرآن كلام الله تعالى في المصاحف مكتوب، وفي القلوب محفوظ، وعلى الألسن مقروء، وصفاته في الأزل غير محدثة ولا مخلوقة هو تأكيد وتأييد أي غير محدثة بإحداثه ولا مخلوقة بخلق غيره. فمن قال إنها مخلوقة أو محدثة أو وقف) أي بأن لا يحكم بأنها قديمة أو حادثة ويؤخر طلب معرفتها ولا يقول آمنت بالله وصفاته على وفق مراده أو شك فيها) أي تردد في هذه المسألة ونحوها سواء يستوي طرفاه أو يترجح ونحوها سواء يستوي طرفاه أو يترجح أحدهما فهو كافر بالله تعالى أي ببعض صفاته وهو مكلف بأن يكون عارفاً بذاته وجميع صفاته، إلا أن الجهل والشك أعني الموجبين للكفر مخصوصان بصفات الله المذكورة من النعوت المسطورة المشهورة، الحياة والقدرة والعلم والكلام والسمع والبصر والإرادة والتخليق والترزيق. والقرآن كلام الله (تعالى أي المنعوت بالفرقان المنزل على عين الأعيان وزين الإنسان إلا أن المراد به ههنا كلامه النفسي ونعته الأنسي، وهذا الإطلاق؛ لأن معناه يفهم بواسطة مبناه، فالمعنى أن كلامه سبحانه الذي نعته المعظم شأنه في المصاحف مكتوب) أي بأيدينا بواسطة نقوش الحروف وأشكال الكلمات وفي القلوب (محفوظ أي نستحضره عند تصور المغيبات بألفاظه المتخيلات (وعلى الألسُن (مقروء) أي بحروفه الملفوظة المسموعة كما هو ظاهر في المشاهدات، وهذا من قولهم: «المقروء قديم والقراءة حادثة».
The statement concerning the Quran. And the Quran is the speech of Allah Almighty, written in the mus'hafs (codices), preserved in hearts, recited on tongues, and His attributes are not originated nor created in eternity – it is an affirmation and confirmation, i.e., not originated by His origination nor created by creation of another. So whoever says they are created or originated, or halts) i.e., by not ruling that they are eternal or temporal and delays seeking knowledge of them and does not say 'I believe in Allah and His attributes according to His will' or doubts them (i.e., wavers in this matter and its like, whether the two sides are equal or one outweighs, and its like whether the two sides are equal or one outweighs) then he is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty, i.e., in some of His attributes. And he is obligated to know His essence and all His attributes, except that ignorance and doubt – I mean the two causes of disbelief – are particular to the mentioned attributes of Allah from the well-known traits recorded and famous: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, bringing into existence (takhlīq), and providing (tarzīq). And the Quran is the speech of Allah (Almighty, i.e., described by the Criterion revealed to the chief of beings and the adornment of mankind, except that what is meant here is His internal speech (kalam nafsi) and its human attribute. And this application is because its meaning is understood through its structure. So the meaning is that His speech, Exalted is He, whose attribute is great, written in the mus'hafs (i.e., in our hands by means of the engravings of letters and forms of words) and preserved in hearts (i.e., we bring it to mind when imagining absent things by means of its imagined words) and recited on tongues (i.e., by its pronounced audible letters as is apparent in observed things). And this is from their saying: 'The recited (al-maqru') is eternal and the recitation (al-qira'a) is temporal.'
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the nature of the Quran. It begins with the heading 'al-qawl fi al-Qur'an' (the statement concerning the Quran). The author then restates the earlier attribute ruling that God's attributes are uncreated, repeating the same conditional and list of attributes. This serves as a reminder that the Quran as kalam Allah (speech of Allah) is among those attributes. The focus then shifts to the Quran specifically: it is Allah's speech, written in mus'hafs, preserved in hearts, recited on tongues. The author clarifies that the Quran meant here is the internal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah, which is eternal, not the physical text or recitation which are created. This is a standard Ash'ari distinction: the meaning of the Quran is uncreated, while its written and recited forms are temporal. The explanation details that the Quran is written 'by means of engravings of letters' and preserved 'when imagining absent things' and recited 'by its pronounced audible letters'. The passage ends with a well-known formula: 'The recited (al-maqru') is eternal and the recitation (al-qira'a) is temporal.' This summarizes the distinction that the Quran as the eternal speech is one thing, while the human act of recitation is another.

Correction: The passage clarifies that while the written and recited forms are temporal, the Quran as Allah's speech (kalam nafsi) is eternal and uncreated.

Key Takeaway
The Quran as Allah's attribute of speech is eternal, while its written, recited, and memorized forms are temporal creations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Divine Attributes Are Uncreated and Eternal
Defines divine attributes as uncreated and states disbelief on denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes are uncreated and eternal, and that denying or doubting this constitutes disbelief in some of His essential attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are eternal, uncreated — to doubt is to disbelieve.

This lesson addresses a foundational principle of Islamic theology: the attributes of Allah are not created or originated; they are eternal just as His essence is eternal. The author declares that whoever claims they are created, suspends judgment, or doubts is a disbeliever. This is a serious matter that requires careful understanding of which attributes are essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully without analysis. Let the author's words set the foundation.
2
Identify the main claim
Notice that the passage begins with a bold statement: Allah's attributes are not originated (muhdatha) nor created (makhluqa). This is the core thesis.
The phrase 'in pre-eternity' (al-azal) emphasizes timelessness.
3
Understand the ruling on denial
The passage lists three forms of denial: saying attributes are created/originated, suspending judgment (waqf), and doubting. Each results in disbelief.
The commentary explains 'waqf' as delaying judgment and not affirming belief.
4
List the essential attributes
The passage ends by naming the attributes that, if denied or doubted, cause disbelief: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, creating, providing.
This shows that not all attributes are treated the same; these are the well-known essential ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفاته في الأزل غير محدثة ولا مخلوقة فمن قال إنها مخلوقة أو محدثة أو وقف أو شك فيها فهو كافر بالله تعالى. وصفاته في الأزل غير محدثة ولا مخلوقة هو تأكيد وتأييد أي غير محدثة بإحداثه ولا مخلوقة بخلق غيره. فمن قال إنها مخلوقة أو محدثة أو وقف أي بأن لا يحكم بأنها قديمة أو حادثة ويؤخر طلب معرفتها ولا يقول آمنت بالله وصفاته على وفق مراده أو شك فيها أي تردد في هذه المسألة ونحوها سواء يستوي طرفاه أو يترجح أحدهما فهو كافر بالله تعالى أي ببعض صفاته وهو مكلف بأن يكون عارفاً بذاته وجميع صفاته، إلا أن الجهل والشك أعني الموجبين للكفر مخصوصان بصفات الله المذكورة من النعوت المسطورة المشهورة، الحياة والقدرة والعلم والكلام والسمع والبصر والإرادة والتخليق والترزيق.
And His attributes in pre-eternity are not originated nor created. So whoever says they are created or originated, or suspends judgment, or doubts them, is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty. And His attributes in pre-eternity are not originated nor created—this is an affirmation and confirmation, meaning they are not originated by His own act of origination nor created by the creation of another. So whoever says they are created or originated, or suspends judgment—meaning that he does not rule that they are eternal or temporal and delays seeking knowledge of them, and does not say 'I believe in Allah and His attributes according to His will'—or doubts them—meaning he wavers in this matter and similar ones, whether the two sides are equal or one is preponderant—then he is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty, meaning in some of His attributes. And he is obligated to know His essence and all His attributes, except that ignorance and doubt—the causes of disbelief—are specific to the mentioned attributes of Allah from the well-known enumerated descriptions: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, creating, and providing.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the nature of divine attributes. It begins by quoting the matn: the attributes of Allah are not originated (muhdatha) nor created (makhluqa) in pre-eternity. Whoever says they are created or originated, or suspends judgment (waqf), or doubts, is a disbeliever (kafir). The sharh then explains that the phrase is an emphasis: they are not originated by Allah's own act of origination, nor created by the creation of another. It elaborates on the meaning of 'waqf' as delaying judgment and not affirming belief in Allah and His attributes according to His will. Doubt is defined as hesitation. The ruling of disbelief applies even if one is uncertain. However, it clarifies that the disbelief is specifically concerning some attributes, and the obligation is to know Allah's essence and all His attributes. But the specific ignorance and doubt that cause disbelief are limited to the well-known attributes listed: life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, creating, and providing. This guards against the error that one might be excused for ignorance of any attribute; rather, these specific ones are essential.

Key Terms
أزل
محدثة
مخلوقة
وقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that doubt or ignorance about any divine attribute is excusable and does not affect faith.
Correction: This passage specifies that doubt or denial of the well-known essential attributes (life, power, knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, will, creating, providing) constitutes disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on one who doubts the eternity of Allah's attributes?
A) He is a disbeliever.
B) He is sinning but remains a believer.
C) He is excused due to ignorance.
D) He must repent but is not a disbeliever.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are eternal and uncreated; doubting these essential attributes makes one a disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever allowed a moment of doubt about any of Allah's essential attributes—like His power or knowledge—to pass without immediately repenting? What will you do the next time such a doubt crosses your mind?
?
If someone asked you right now whether Allah's attributes are created or eternal, would your answer be immediate and firm, or would you hesitate? What does your hesitation reveal about the state of your faith?
?
The passage lists nine attributes you must affirm. Is there even one among them that you have not truly reflected upon or internalized? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen your conviction in that attribute?

The Quran's Revelation: Gradual and Renewed, but Eternal
Explains the gradual, renewed revelation of the Quran and contrasts it with Allah's eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran's revelation is a gradual sending down via letters and words, and that it is renewed only in its descent, not in Allah's eternal speech.

Core Idea
Revelation is renewed; Allah's speech is eternal and unchanged.

This passage begins by discussing the nature of the Quran's revelation. It clarifies that the Quran was sent down to the Prophet gradually and repeatedly, using letters and words. The author emphasizes that this 'renewal' applies only to the act of sending down, not to the divine attribute of speech itself, which is eternal and transcends change. Let's examine the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the distinction between 'sent down' and 'renewed'.
The verse from al-Anbiya' is key.
2
Identify the two aspects
The passage mentions two aspects: the temporal revelation (muhdath fi al-inzal) and the eternal self-subsisting speech (kalam nafsi). Understand how they relate.
3
Reflect on the verse
Look at the Qur'anic verse cited and how the author interprets 'muhdath' as renewed in sending down. This guards against the misconception that Allah's speech itself changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم منزل بالتخفيف والتشديد وهو الأولى لنزوله مدرجاً ومكرراً، والمعنى أنه نزل عليه بواسطة الحروف المفردات والمركبات في الحالات المختلفات، وهذا معنى قوله سبحانه: مَا يَأْتِيهِمْ مِنْ ذِكْرٍ مِنْ تَبِهِمْ مُّحْدَثٍ إِلَّا اسْتَمَعُوهُ وَهُمْ يَلْعَبُونَ ﴾ [الانبيا : ٢]، أي محدث في الإنزال، وإلا فكلامه النفسي منزه عن الانتقال. ولفظنا بالقرآن مخلوق، وكتابتنا له مخلوقة، وقراءتنا له مخلوقة) وهذا كالتأكيد لقوله: «لفظنا ولا يبعد أن يراد بالقراءة تصور مبانيه وتقرر معانيه من غير التلفظ بما فيه، ولعله لهذا المعنى لم يقل وحفظنا له مخلوق، وذلك لأنها كلها من أفعالنا وفعل المخلوق مخلوق. (والقرآن أي كلامه النفسي ونعته القدسي (غير) (مخلوق) أي ولا حال في المصاحف ولا غيرها، وذلك أن كل من يأمر وينهى ويخبر عن ما مضى يجد في نفسه معنى يدل عليه بالعبارة أو يشير إليه بالكتابة أو الإشارة. ثم اعلم أن مذهب الأشعري أنه يجوز أن يسمع الكلام النفسي، أي بطريق خرق العادة
And upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, it is sent down—with tashdid (lit. 'sent down') or takhif (lit. 'descended')—and the former is preferable because it came down gradually and repeatedly. The meaning is that it descended upon him by means of individual and compound letters in various circumstances. This is the meaning of His saying: 'There comes not to them a renewed reminder from their Lord except they listen to it while they play' [al-Anbiya' 21:2]—meaning renewed in its sending down; otherwise, His self-subsisting speech is transcendent above transition. And our pronunciation (lafz) of the Quran is created, our writing of it is created, and our recitation (qira'a) of it is created. This is like an affirmation of his statement 'our pronunciation' and it is not far that by 'recitation' is meant the conceptualization of its structures and the establishment of its meanings without uttering its words. Perhaps for this meaning he did not say 'our memorization of it is created,' because all of these are from our actions, and the action of the created is created. And the Quran—i.e., His self-subsisting speech and His holy attribute—is not created, nor does it inhere in the manuscripts or anything else. That is because everyone who commands, forbids, and informs about the past finds within himself a meaning that he indicates by expression or points to by writing or gesture. Then know that the school of al-Ash'ari is that it is permissible to hear the self-subsisting speech, that is, by way of breaking the custom (khariq al-'ada).
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage covers multiple related points. First, it discusses the revelation (tanzil) of the Quran, stating that the Prophet received it gradually via letters and words. It clarifies that the sending down is temporal (muhdath fi al-inzal), while the eternal self-subsisting speech is beyond transition. Second, it affirms that our pronunciation, writing, and recitation of the Quran are created because they are our actions. It notes that 'recitation' might mean conceptualization without vocalization, which explains why 'memorization' is not mentioned as created—it is a mental act. Third, it reiterates that the Quran (eternal speech) is not created and does not inhere in manuscripts or other physical things. It draws an analogy: any person who commands, forbids, or informs finds in himself a meaning that he expresses. Finally, it mentions the Ash'ari view that it is possible to hear the eternal speech—supernaturally, as a miracle. This passage reinforces the distinction between the uncreated attribute and created human acts, and introduces a theological nuance about the possibility of directly hearing the eternal speech.

Key Terms
منزل
محدث
كلام نفسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the Quran was revealed gradually, Allah's speech itself changes over time.
Correction: This passage clarifies that only the sending down is renewed; the eternal speech is beyond transition.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does 'muhdath' (renewed) in the verse refer to?
A) The eternal speech of Allah
B) The sending down of the Quran
C) The letters and words
D) The Prophet's recitation

Key Takeaway
The Quran's revelation is renewed in its descent, but Allah's eternal speech remains unchanged.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran is the eternal speech of Allah, what does that mean for how you recite it? Do you approach it as a temporary message or as the very words of the Eternal?
?
The revelation came gradually over 23 years. Are you patient with your own understanding of the Quran, or do you rush through it as if it were a single moment?
?
Allah's speech is unchangeable, yet it addresses you directly in your specific situation. How does this truth challenge the way you live today? Will you let this passage change how you listen to the Quran tomorrow?

Our Created Recitation and the Uncreated Quran
Affirms that human acts related to the Quran are created, while the Quran itself is uncreated and not immanent in physical objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that our pronunciation, writing, and recitation of the Quran are created acts, while the Quran itself (as Allah's eternal speech) is uncreated and does not inhere in physical things.

Core Idea
Human recitation is created; the Quran is not.

Having established the nature of revelation, the author now turns to the distinction between human acts related to the Quran and the Quran itself. He affirms that our pronunciation, writing, and recitation are created because they are our actions. He also clarifies that the Quran—the eternal speech—is not created and does not dwell in manuscripts or other physical objects. Let's dive into this important theological distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the list: pronunciation, writing, recitation—all created.
Recitation may refer to conceptualization, not vocalization.
2
Understand the analogy
The author gives an analogy: any person who commands or forbids finds a meaning in himself that he expresses. This helps understand that the eternal speech is a meaning, not the physical words.
3
Contrast with the Quran itself
Notice that the Quran (eternal speech) is not created and does not inhere in manuscripts. This guards against the view that the Quran we hold is the uncreated speech.

Source Text

Hearing the Eternal Speech (Ash'ari View)
States the Ash'ari view that Allah's eternal speech can be heard supernaturally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that it is possible to hear Allah's eternal self-subsisting speech through a miracle (khariq al-'ada).

Core Idea
Allah's eternal speech can be heard supernaturally.

The passage concludes with an important theological point from the Ash'ari school: it is possible for someone to hear the eternal speech of Allah, but this happens through a breach of natural custom (khariq al-'ada), i.e., a miracle. This is a subtle but significant claim about the nature of divine speech and its perception. Let's examine this final statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding sentence
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the key phrase: 'by way of breaking the custom'.
This is a distinct Ash'ari teaching.
2
Understand the implication
Think about what it means to hear the eternal speech. It is not the same as hearing the recited Quran. It is a direct perception of the attribute, possible only through a miracle.
3
Connect to the previous discussion
This builds on the distinction between created recitation and uncreated speech. Hearing the latter is extraordinary.

Source Text

Abu Hanifa's Wasiyya on the Uncreated Qur'an
Abu Hanifa affirms the Qur'an as uncreated attribute while defining created physical elements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hanifa's distinction between the uncreated speech of Allah and the created physical forms of the Qur'an, as stated in his al-Wasiyya.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's meaning is uncreated, its letters and ink are created.

Abu Hanifa's al-Wasiyya is a foundational text of Ahl al-Sunna. In this passage, he lays out the precise boundary: the Qur'an is Allah's eternal speech, but the physical letters, paper, and sounds are human acts. Let's examine his exact words.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Notice the structure: affirmations first, then distinctions.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا هو ولا غيره' (neither He nor other than He).
2
Identify the two categories
Find where Abu Hanifa distinguishes between what is attributed to Allah (speech, attribute) and what is attributed to creation (letters, writing, paper).
The words 'مخلوقة' (created) and 'غير مخلوق' (uncreated) are key.
3
Understand the logical consequence
Notice that calling the speech itself created is an act of disbelief. This shows how seriously this distinction is held.
The phrase 'فمن قال بأن كلام الله تعالى مخلوق فهو كافر' is the conclusion.
4
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself why the physical forms are created. The passage says because they are actions of servants. Reflect on how this distinguishes the Maturidi view from other schools.
This distinction preserved the transcendence of Allah's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال الإمام الأعظم في كتابه "الوصية": نقر بأن القرآن كلام الله تعالى ووحيه وتنزيله وصفته لا هو ولا غيره، بل هو صفته على التحقيق مكتوب في المصاحف مقروء بالألسن محفوظ في الصدور غير حال فيها، والحروف والحركات والكاغذ والكتابة كلها مخلوقة لأنها أفعال العباد، وكلام الله سبحانه وتعالى غير مخلوق، لأن الكتابة والحروف والكلمات والآيات كله آلة القرآن لحاجة العباد إليها وكلام الله تعالى قائم بذاته ومعناه مفهوم بهذه الأشياء، فمن قال بأن كلام الله تعالى مخلوق فهو كافر بالله العظيم والله تعالى معبود ولا يزال عما كان وكلامه مقروء ومكتوب ومحفوظ من غير مزايلة عنه.
And indeed Imam al-A'zam said in his book 'al-Wasiyya': We affirm that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah, Exalted, and His revelation, and His descent, and His attribute; it is not He nor other than He, rather it is His attribute in reality, written in the mus'hafs, recited by tongues, preserved in chests, not residing in them. The letters, movements, paper, and writing are all created because they are actions of servants. The speech of Allah, Glorified and Exalted, is uncreated, because writing, letters, words, and verses are all instruments of the Qur'an due to the need of servants for them, while the speech of Allah, Exalted, subsists by His essence, and its meaning is understood through these things. So whoever says that the speech of Allah, Exalted, is created is a disbeliever in Allah the Magnificent. Allah, Exalted, is worshipped and remains as He has always been, and His speech is recited, written, and preserved without separation from Him.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a direct quotation from Abu Hanifa's work 'al-Wasiyya', which is a core text of Maturidi creed. The author uses it to establish the orthodox position on the Qur'an. Abu Hanifa declares that the Qur'an is God's speech, revelation, and attribute – it is neither identical to God nor something other than Him, but a real attribute. Then he makes a crucial distinction: the physical manifestations (letters, sounds, paper, writing) are all created because they are human actions. The eternal speech of God is uncreated and subsists in God's essence; the written and recited forms are instruments to convey its meaning. Anyone who claims the speech itself is created is a disbeliever. The passage ends by affirming that God remains as He always was, and His speech is recited and written without being separated from Him.

Key Terms
كلام الله
صفته
مخلوق
غير مخلوق
الوصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The written or recited Qur'an is itself uncreated.
Correction: Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the meaning/attribute is uncreated, the physical letters and sounds are created.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa in al-Wasiyya, what are the letters and writing of the Qur'an?
A) Uncreated
B) Created because they are actions of servants
C) Part of God's speech
D) Eternal

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's al-Wasiyya clarifies that the Qur'an's eternal speech is uncreated, while its physical letters, sounds, and writings are created human acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a mus-haf, do you treat it as the eternal speech of Allah Himself, or do you view it as just a book? How would your reverence change if you truly internalized that the meaning is uncreated and the paper is merely a tool?
?
The passage declares that anyone who says Allah's speech is created is a disbeliever. Have you ever allowed yourself to think of the Qur'an as a human composition or a product of history? What must you do to guard your heart from such doubts and affirm the Qur'an as Allah's uncreated attribute?
?
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between uncreated meaning and created letters. In your own recitation, do you focus more on the physical act of reading or on connecting with the eternal meaning? What practical step can you take today to prioritize the uncreated word over the created form?

The Real Dispute: Kalam Nafsi vs. Created Words
Identifies the core issue with Mu'tazila as affirming or denying internal eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise point of disagreement between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila regarding God's speech, and why the doctrine of kalam nafsi is necessary.

Core Idea
The real dispute is not about words, but about God's inner eternal speech.

In this passage, the author cuts through a common misconception. Many assume the controversy over God's speech is about the Arabic text being created or uncreated. But here he clarifies that both sides agree the words and letters are created. The actual point of contention is deeper: whether God possesses an eternal attribute of speech that subsists in His essence—what is called kalam nafsi. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument come through.
Notice how the author states the core issue first.
2
Identify the common ground
Find where the author says 'we do not say the words are eternal, and they do not say internal speech is originated.' This shows both sides agree on something.
This common ground is crucial to understanding the real dispute.
3
Understand 'kalam nafsi'
The term 'kalam nafsi' means internal speech — an eternal attribute of God. Contrast this with the created letters and sounds.
Kalam nafsi is not heard or written; it is God's eternal attribute of speech.
4
Examine the evidence
The author gives evidence from consensus and prophetic reports that God is Mutakallim. Reflect on why this evidence leads to the conclusion.
The evidence shows that God speaking implies an attribute, not just creating sounds.
5
Follow the conclusion
The author concludes that since created speech cannot subsist in God's essence, the speech must be eternal internal speech (al-nafsi al-qadim).
This is the Sunni doctrine: God's speech is an eternal attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تحقيق الخلاف بيننا وبين المعتزلة يرجع إلى إثبات الكلام النفسي ونفيه، وإلا فنحن لا نقول بقدم الألفاظ والحروف، وهم لا يقولون بحدوث الكلام النفسي، ودليلنا ما ر أنه ثبت بالإجماع وتواتر النقل عن الأنبياء عليهم السلام أنه متكلم، ولا معنى له سوى أنه متصف بالكلام ويمتنع قيام اللفظ الحادث بذاته الكريم، فتعين النفسي القديم.
Then the reality of the dispute between us and the Mu'tazila returns to the affirmation and denial of internal speech (al-kalam al-nafsi). Otherwise, we do not say the words and letters are eternal, and they do not say that internal speech is originated. Our evidence is what has been established by consensus and successive transmission from the prophets, peace be upon them, that He is Mutakallim (speaking). And there is no meaning to that except that He is described with speech, and it is impossible for originated utterance to subsist in His noble essence. Thus the eternal internal speech (al-nafsi al-qadim) is necessarily affirmed.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a key summary of the controversy. The author states that the core issue is whether God has an eternal attribute of speech subsisting in His essence (kalam nafsi) or not. Both sides agree that the spoken letters and sounds are created (hadith). The Mu'tazila deny internal speech, claiming that God's being 'mutakallim' means He creates speech in some substrate. The author presents the evidence: consensus and prophetic reports confirm that God is 'mutakallim'. The only coherent meaning is that He possesses speech as an attribute. Since originated sounds cannot subsist in God's essence, the speech must be eternal and internal (nafsi). Thus the doctrine of kalam nafsi is concluded.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي
الكلام القديم
متكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ahl al-Sunna believe the recited words of the Quran are eternal.
Correction: The author clarifies that both sides agree the letters and words are created; the real dispute is about the existence of an eternal attribute of speech in God's essence.

Checkpoint
What is the core issue of disagreement between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila regarding speech?
A) The eternity of words and letters
B) Affirming or denying internal speech
C) The createdness of the Quran
D) Its miraculous nature

Key Takeaway
The true point of contention regarding God's speech is whether He possesses an eternal internal attribute of speech, not whether the words are created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You recite the Quran daily and believe it is the word of God. But if the physical words you utter are not eternal but only a created expression, what is it that makes your heart tremble when you hear them? What will you change in your recitation to consciously seek that connection?
?
The author argues that it is impossible for originated speech to subsist in God. Yet you might still conceive of God speaking in a human way. When you say 'Allah spoke to Musa,' do you picture God uttering sounds? How does the doctrine of internal speech correct that mental image? Will you remind yourself during the recitation of the Quran that its source is an eternal, non-created attribute? What practical step can you take to cultivate this awareness?

Consensus on Divine Attributes: Neither He Nor Other Than Him
States consensus that every attribute of God is neither identical to Him nor distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early Muslim consensus that each divine attribute is neither identical to Allah's essence nor something entirely distinct.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are the middle path between identifying them with Allah and separating them.

The early generations of Muslims—Companions, Successors, and later scholars—agreed on a precise formulation regarding the divine attributes. They affirmed that every attribute of Allah, such as knowledge or power, is not the same as His essence, nor is it a completely separate thing. This lesson explains that consensus and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the original Arabic statement and its English translation. Notice the concise way the consensus is introduced and then explained.
The passage is short but packs a key doctrinal rule.
2
Identify the consensus statement
Find the phrase 'قد أجمعوا على أن كل صفة من صفات الله تعالى لا هو ولا غيره'. This is the core claim: the scholars agreed that every attribute is 'neither He nor other than He'.
This consensus is an authoritative source for the middle position.
3
Understand 'لا هو ولا غيره'
Reflect on the meaning of this phrase. It means the attribute is not identical to Allah's essence (so it is not 'He'), nor is it a separate created thing (so it is not 'other than He'). It is a real meaning that subsists in the essence without being the essence itself.
This avoids two extremes: likening Allah to creation (tashbih) and stripping Him of attributes (ta'til).
4
Connect to the broader methodology
Consider why the early scholars considered this consensus important. It establishes a safe, scripturally grounded way to talk about Allah's attributes without falling into error.
This consensus is a foundation for later discussions in 'ilm al-kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاعلم أن الصحابة والتابعين وغيرهم من المجتهدين رضوان الله تعالى عليهم أجمعين، قد أجمعوا على أن كل صفة من صفات الله تعالى لا هو ولا غيره، كذا ذكره الشارح؛ والمعنى أنها لا هو ولا غيره.
Know that the Companions, Successors, and other mujtahidun, may Allah be pleased with them all, have agreed (ajma'u) that every attribute of Allah, Exalted, is neither He nor other than He. Thus the commentator (al-sharih) mentioned it; and the meaning is that it is neither He nor other than He.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a brief statement of consensus (ijma') among the early generations. The author asserts that the Companions, Successors, and later qualified scholars unanimously held that each divine attribute (such as knowledge, power, speech) is neither identical to God's essence (lahu) nor something entirely separate (ghayruhu). This is the middle path between anthropomorphism (which makes attributes like human ones) and negation (which strips God of attributes). The commentator quoted simply repeats the phrase: 'Neither He nor other than Him'.

Key Terms
الصحابة
التابعين
إجماع
لا هو ولا غيره

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that attributes of Allah are either exactly His essence (so they are not real in any sense) or completely separate entities (like created things).
Correction: The early consensus rejects both extremes. Each attribute is a real meaning that subsists in the essence, but it is not the essence itself, nor is it an independent thing. This is captured by 'la huwa wa la ghayruhu'.

Checkpoint
ما هو إجماع الصحابة والتابعين في صفات الله تعالى؟
A) إنها عين الذات
B) إنها غير الذات
C) إنها لا هي عين الذات ولا غيرها
D) إنها قديمة

Key Takeaway
The early Muslim consensus affirms that every divine attribute is neither the same as Allah's essence nor a separate entity, a middle path that preserves both divine unity and the reality of attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's attributes, do you find yourself leaning towards making them identical to His essence (risking denial of multiplicity) or seeing them as separate entities (risking shirk)? Which side do you naturally gravitate to, and why?
?
The early Muslims agreed on this precise formulation 'neither He nor other'. Are you satisfied that your own belief matches theirs, or do you have hidden reservations? Be honest—what would it take for you to fully accept this middle path?
?
If you truly hold that Allah's attributes are neither His essence nor other, how should that affect the way you speak about His mercy, anger, or love? Does your daily talk reflect this balance, or do you sometimes describe His attributes casually, without guarding against extremes?

The Real Point of Contention with the Mu'tazila
Clarifies the real point of dispute regarding divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the real dispute between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila about divine speech is not about whether the Qur'an is created or uncreated, but about affirming or denying an eternal attribute of inner speech (kalam nafsi).

Core Idea
The dispute is not about words being created, but about an eternal attribute of speech.

The author begins by clearing a common misconception: the famous hadith threatening disbelief for saying the Qur'an is created is baseless. He then cuts to the heart of the matter: the real disagreement with the Mu'tazila is whether God possesses an eternal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi) or not. Both sides agree that the uttered words and letters are created, so the debate is solely about the inner, eternal speech.

Guided Path
1
Understand the false hadith
The opening sentence dismisses a hadith as baseless.
2
Identify the real dispute
The dispute is about affirming or negating kalam nafsi, not about creation of words.
3
Note the common ground
Both sides agree that words/letters are created; Ahl al-Sunna say inner speech is eternal, Mu'tazila deny that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال إنه مخلوق فهو كافر بالله العظيم فهو لا أصل له. ثم تحقيق الخلاف بيننا وبين المعتزلة يرجع إلى إثبات الكلام النفسي ونفيه، وإلا فنحن لا نقول بقدم الألفاظ والحروف، وهم لا يقولون بحدوث الكلام النفسي، ودليلنا ما ر أنه ثبت بالإجماع وتواتر النقل عن الأنبياء عليهم السلام أنه متكلم، ولا معنى له سوى أنه متصف بالكلام ويمتنع قيام اللفظ الحادث بذاته الكريم، فتعين النفسي القديم. وأما استدلالهم بأن القرآن متصف بما هو من صفات المخلوق وسمات الحدوث من التأليف والتنظيم والنزول والتنزيل وكونه عربياً مسموعاً فصيحاً معجزاً إلى غير ذلك، فإنما يقوم حجة على الحنابلة لا علينا؛ لأنا قائلون بحدوث النظم أيضاً، وإنما الكلام في معنى القديم. والمعتزلة لما لم يمكنهم إنكار كونه متكلما ذهبوا إلى أنه متكلم بمعنى موجد الأصوات والحروف في محالها وأشكال الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ وإن لم يقرأ على اختلاف قامت به الحركة لا من أوجدها. وأما إذا كان في الآية قراءتان، فإن كان لكل قراءة معنى غير الأخرى، فالله تعالى تكلم بهما جميعا وصارت القراءتان بمنزلة الآيتين وإن كانت القراءتان معناهما واحد فالله تعالى تكلم بأحدهما ورخص بأن يقرأ بهما جميعا كما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث.
And whoever says that it (the Qur'an) is created, then he is a disbeliever in Allah the Great—it has no basis. Then the verification of the dispute between us and the Mu'tazila revolves around affirming eternal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī) and negating it. Otherwise, we do not affirm pre-eternity of words and letters, and they do not affirm temporality of eternal speech. Our proof is that it is established by consensus and successive transmission from the prophets, peace be upon them, that He is speaking (mutakallim). There is no meaning to this except that He is described by speech, and it is impossible for temporal utterance to subsist in His noble essence. So the eternal (al-qadīm) inner speech is determined. As for their argument that the Qur'an is described with attributes of the created and marks of temporality, such as composition, organization, descent, revelation, being Arabic, audible, eloquent, miraculous, etc., it is only an argument against the Hanabila, not against us; for we also affirm the temporality of organization (al-naẓm). The discussion is only about the meaning of the eternal (al-qadīm). The Mu'tazila, since they could not deny that He is speaking, went to the position that He is speaking in the sense of creating sounds and letters in their places and forms of writing in the Preserved Tablet, even if not read—according to different views—the movement subsists in it, not the One who caused it. As for when there are two readings (qirā'atān) in a verse: if each reading has a meaning different from the other, then Allah Almighty spoke with both of them, and the two readings become like two verses; but if the two readings have the same meaning, then Allah Almighty spoke with one of them and permitted recitation with both, as mentioned by al-Faqīh Abū al-Layth.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage begins by asserting that the hadith saying 'Whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever' has no authentic basis. Then it clarifies the real point of contention between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila: the dispute is about affirming or denying internal eternal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī). Both sides agree that the Qur'an's words and letters are created; the Mu'tazila deny that God has an eternal attribute of speech, while Ahl al-Sunna affirm it. The proof given is: God is described as 'speaking' by consensus and tawātur. Speech cannot be a temporal utterance subsisting in God because that would imply change in His essence. Therefore, the speech must be an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. The author then addresses the Mu'tazila's argument that the Qur'an displays temporal characteristics like composition and descent. This argument only refutes the view that the words themselves are eternal—a view held by some Hanabila—but it does not refute the Sunni position that the attribute of speech is eternal while the verbal expression is created. The Mu'tazila, unable to deny that God is 'speaking', reinterpret it as 'creating sounds and letters' in bodies or on the Preserved Tablet. Finally, the passage discusses cases where a verse has two canonical readings (qirā'āt): if they differ in meaning, God literally spoke both; if they have the same meaning, He spoke one and permitted both for ease.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي
القدم
الحدوث
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dispute is about whether the Qur'an as we recite it is created or uncreated.
Correction: The passage clarifies that both sides agree the uttered words are created; the real dispute is about the eternal attribute of inner speech.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the real point of dispute between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila?
A) Whether the Qur'an is created or uncreated
B) Whether God has an eternal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi) or not
C) Whether the Qur'an is Arabic and miraculous
D) Whether the Prophet received revelation in clear Arabic

Key Takeaway
The real disagreement is not about creation of the Qur'anic text, but about whether God has an eternal attribute of speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is an eternal attribute, then every word of the Qur'an is an expression of His eternal nature. Does your reverence for the Qur'an reflect that reality? What specific change will you make in your daily recitation to remind yourself that you are hearing God's own eternal speech?
?
The Mu'tazila denied eternal speech because they saw it as a threat to God's oneness. Have you ever rejected a truth about God because it seemed to conflict with your limited understanding? Are there any attributes of God you find hard to accept? Take a moment to submit your intellect to revelation.
?
This lesson shows that the real disagreement is not about words but about the essence of God. When you use the Qur'an to justify your opinions, are you aware that you are using God's eternal attribute? How can you ensure you approach the Qur'an with more awe and less presumption?

Proof for God's Eternal Inner Speech
Presents the proof for eternal inner speech (kalam nafsi).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that God possesses an eternal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi), based on consensus and the impossibility of temporal speech residing in God's essence.

Core Idea
God is called 'speaker' by consensus; temporal speech cannot be in God, so it must be eternal.

Having clarified that the real issue is the existence of an eternal speech attribute, the author now provides the proof. He argues from the undoubted fact that God is described as 'speaking' across all revelations. Since it is impossible for a temporal utterance (like a sound or word) to subsist in God's essence, the speech that describes Him must be an eternal attribute. This establishes the doctrine of kalam nafsi.

Guided Path
1
Establish that God is described as 'speaking'
The proof begins with the undeniable fact, established by consensus and prophetic revelation, that God is mutakallim (speaking).
2
Understand the impossibility
It is impossible for temporal utterance (hādith) to subsist in God's essence because that would imply change.
3
Conclude eternal speech
Therefore, the speech that is God's attribute must be eternal (qadīm) and internal (nafsī).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Mu'tazila Position on Divine Speech and the Two Readings
Explains Mu'tazila view on divine speech and the ruling on dual readings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's alternative explanation of God being 'speaking' (as creator of sounds) and the ruling on two canonical readings (qirā'āt) with same or different meanings.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila say God creates speech; two readings with same meaning are from one divine utterance.

After establishing the Sunni proof for kalam nafsi, the author describes the Mu'tazila's position: they could not deny that God is 'speaking', so they reinterpreted it as meaning that God creates sounds and letters in some location (like the Preserved Tablet) rather than possessing an eternal attribute. The author then addresses a related issue: when a verse has two canonical readings, if they differ in meaning, God spoke both; if they have the same meaning, He spoke one and permitted the other.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila position
They say God is 'speaking' in the sense of creating sounds and letters, not as an attribute.
2
Note the details
They differ on whether the movement (sounds) subsists in the created thing or not.
3
Apply the rule for two readings
If readings have different meanings, God spoke both; if same meaning, He spoke one but permitted both.
4
Recognise the authority
This ruling is attributed to al-Faqih Abu al-Layth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال إنه مخلوق فهو كافر بالله العظيم فهو لا أصل له. ثم تحقيق الخلاف بيننا وبين المعتزلة يرجع إلى إثبات الكلام النفسي ونفيه، وإلا فنحن لا نقول بقدم الألفاظ والحروف، وهم لا يقولون بحدوث الكلام النفسي، ودليلنا ما ر أنه ثبت بالإجماع وتواتر النقل عن الأنبياء عليهم السلام أنه متكلم، ولا معنى له سوى أنه متصف بالكلام ويمتنع قيام اللفظ الحادث بذاته الكريم، فتعين النفسي القديم. وأما استدلالهم بأن القرآن متصف بما هو من صفات المخلوق وسمات الحدوث من التأليف والتنظيم والنزول والتنزيل وكونه عربياً مسموعاً فصيحاً معجزاً إلى غير ذلك، فإنما يقوم حجة على الحنابلة لا علينا؛ لأنا قائلون بحدوث النظم أيضاً، وإنما الكلام في معنى القديم. والمعتزلة لما لم يمكنهم إنكار كونه متكلما ذهبوا إلى أنه متكلم بمعنى موجد الأصوات والحروف في محالها وأشكال الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ وإن لم يقرأ على اختلاف قامت به الحركة لا من أوجدها. وأما إذا كان في الآية قراءتان، فإن كان لكل قراءة معنى غير الأخرى، فالله تعالى تكلم بهما جميعا وصارت القراءتان بمنزلة الآيتين وإن كانت القراءتان معناهما واحد فالله تعالى تكلم بأحدهما ورخص بأن يقرأ بهما جميعا كما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث.
And whoever says that it (the Qur'an) is created, then he is a disbeliever in Allah the Great—it has no basis. Then the verification of the dispute between us and the Mu'tazila revolves around affirming eternal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī) and negating it. Otherwise, we do not affirm pre-eternity of words and letters, and they do not affirm temporality of eternal speech. Our proof is that it is established by consensus and successive transmission from the prophets, peace be upon them, that He is speaking (mutakallim). There is no meaning to this except that He is described by speech, and it is impossible for temporal utterance to subsist in His noble essence. So the eternal (al-qadīm) inner speech is determined. As for their argument that the Qur'an is described with attributes of the created and marks of temporality, such as composition, organization, descent, revelation, being Arabic, audible, eloquent, miraculous, etc., it is only an argument against the Hanabila, not against us; for we also affirm the temporality of organization (al-naẓm). The discussion is only about the meaning of the eternal (al-qadīm). The Mu'tazila, since they could not deny that He is speaking, went to the position that He is speaking in the sense of creating sounds and letters in their places and forms of writing in the Preserved Tablet, even if not read—according to different views—the movement subsists in it, not the One who caused it. As for when there are two readings (qirā'atān) in a verse: if each reading has a meaning different from the other, then Allah Almighty spoke with both of them, and the two readings become like two verses; but if the two readings have the same meaning, then Allah Almighty spoke with one of them and permitted recitation with both, as mentioned by al-Faqīh Abū al-Layth.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage begins by asserting that the hadith saying 'Whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever' has no authentic basis. Then it clarifies the real point of contention between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila: the dispute is about affirming or denying internal eternal speech (al-kalām al-nafsī). Both sides agree that the Qur'an's words and letters are created; the Mu'tazila deny that God has an eternal attribute of speech, while Ahl al-Sunna affirm it. The proof given is: God is described as 'speaking' by consensus and tawātur. Speech cannot be a temporal utterance subsisting in God because that would imply change in His essence. Therefore, the speech must be an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. The author then addresses the Mu'tazila's argument that the Qur'an displays temporal characteristics like composition and descent. This argument only refutes the view that the words themselves are eternal—a view held by some Hanabila—but it does not refute the Sunni position that the attribute of speech is eternal while the verbal expression is created. The Mu'tazila, unable to deny that God is 'speaking', reinterpret it as 'creating sounds and letters' in bodies or on the Preserved Tablet. Finally, the passage discusses cases where a verse has two canonical readings (qirā'āt): if they differ in meaning, God literally spoke both; if they have the same meaning, He spoke one and permitted both for ease.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
القراءتان
اللوح المحفوظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All two-readings cases are considered multiple revelations from God.
Correction: The passage distinguishes: if meanings differ, both are from God; if same meaning, only one is from God, the other is a permissible variant.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rule when two canonical readings of a verse have different meanings?
A) Only one reading is authentic
B) God spoke both readings, and they are like two separate verses
C) The reader may choose either
D) The readings are considered mistakes

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila reinterpret 'speaker' as 'creator of sounds', and two readings with different meanings are both divine speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite a verse with multiple qirā'āt, do you ponder that each variant with a different meaning is a distinct revelation from Allah? How might this awareness transform your recitation from routine to reverent engagement with His words? Will you pause next time to reflect on which reading you are reciting and what it means?
?
The Mu'tazila redefined God's speech to fit their rational framework. Is there any attribute of Allah that you have unconsciously minimized or reinterpreted because it felt uncomfortable or difficult to accept? What would it cost you to submit fully to His attributes as revealed, even if they transcend your reason?
?
If the Qur'an is only created speech, as the Mu'tazila claim, then it is not eternal and could be subject to change or loss. Do you truly believe that the words you recite are the uncreated, eternal speech of Allah? When doubts whisper, what anchors you to the truth? Will you commit to seeking knowledge that strengthens your conviction in the divine origin of the Qur'an?
