God's Attributes: Incomparable to Human Attributes
The author elaborates on the incomparability of God's attributes of knowledge, power, sight, and hearing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's attributes of knowledge, power, sight, and hearing are fundamentally different from human attributes, being essential, eternal, and independent of instruments and objects.

Core Idea
God's attributes are not like ours—they are essential, eternal, and free from creaturely limitations.

This passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar explains a core principle: when we say God knows, sees, or hears, we mean something entirely different from human experience. The author contrasts human limitations with divine perfection, using a dream analogy to show that God's sight and hearing do not depend on the existence of objects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a repetitive pattern for each attribute.
2
Identify the four attributes
The passage presents four divine attributes: knowledge, power, sight, and hearing. For each, find the phrase 'not like our...' and the explanation of the difference.
3
Understand the contrasts
For each attribute, note how human attributes are limited (instruments, acquisition, dependence on objects) while God's are essential, eternal, and absolute.
Pay special attention to the dream analogy for sight and hearing.
4
Reflect on the dream analogy
The author uses a dream analogy to show that God's seeing and hearing are not dependent on the existence of objects. Ask yourself: what does this teach about the nature of divine attributes?
This counters a common misconception that God's attributes are like ours.
5
Apply the principle
The principle of incomparability is foundational for tawhid. Consider how this applies to other attributes like speech or will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعلم لا كعلمنا ويقدر لا كقدرتنا، ويرى لا كرؤيتنا، ويسمع لا كسمعنا، ونعت الخلق من العلم والقدرة والرؤية والكلام والسمع ونحوه، كما بينه بقوله (يعلم) أي تعالى، كما في نسخة (لا) (كعلمنا أي معشر الخلق، فإنا نعلم الأشياء بآلات وتصور صور حاصلات في أذهاننا بقدر أفهامنا وإعلامنا، والله تعالى يعلم حقائق الأشياء كلّيها وجزئيها ظاهرها ومخفيها بعلم ذاتي صمدي أزلي أبدي. ويقدر أي الله سبحانه لا كقدرتنا لأن قدرته تعالى قديمة لا بآلة ولا بمشاركة وهو على كل شيء قدير، ونحن لا نقدر إلا على بعض الأشياء بالإقدار، وذلك المقدار أيضاً بالآلات والأعوان والأنصار ، وأما هو سبحانه وتعالى ففاعل مختار وقادر حكيم مدبّر بقدرة واختيار. ويرى أي هو سبحانه، لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ يَعْلَمْ بِأَنَّ اللَّهَ يَرَى﴾ [العلق: ١٤]. لا كرؤيتنا ويسمع لا كسمعنا فإنا نرى الأشكال والألوان المختلفة ونسمع الأصوات والكلمات المؤتلفة بالآلات المخلوقة في الأعضاء المركبة على وفق إبصاره لأبصارنا وإسماعه لأسماعنا كما ورد في الدعا: ((اللهم متعنا بأسماعنا وأبصارنا ما أحييتنا)). والله سبحانه يرى الأشكال والألوان والهيئات المختلفة بإبصاره الذي هو صفته علی نعت اقتداره، ويسمع الأصوات والكلمات المفردات والمركبات بسمعه الذي هو نعته لا بآلة من الآلات ولا بمشاركة غيره من الكائنات، وإن رؤيته للمرئيات وسمعه للمسموعات قديمة بالذات وإن كان المرئي والمسموع من الحادثات على ما سبق بيانه من سائر الصفات من أن تأخر المتعلق الحادث لا ينافي تقدم المتعلق القديم ألا ترى أنك ترى في حالة نومك بقوى بطون دماغك في حالة رؤياك أشكالا وألوانا وتسمع أصواتا وأفنانا ولا شكل ولا لون بحاصل ولا حاضر وبعد زمان غابر ترى تلك الألوان والأشكال، وتسمع تلك الأصوات والأقوال، في حال يقظتك
He knows not like our knowledge, and He has power not like our power, and He sees not like our sight, and He hears not like our hearing. And the attributes of creation from knowledge, power, sight, speech, hearing, etc., as He explained by His saying 'He knows' i.e., the Exalted, as in one copy: 'not like our knowledge, i.e., O community of creatures. For we know things by instruments and the conception of forms occurring in our minds according to the capacity of our understandings and what we are taught. And God the Exalted knows the realities of things, universal and particular, apparent and hidden, with a knowledge that is essential, self-subsistent, eternal, without beginning and without end. And He has power i.e., God the Glorified, not like our power, because His power is eternal, without instrument and without participation, and He is over all things powerful. We have power only over some things by being given power, and that amount is also by instruments, aides, and supporters. As for Him, Glorified and Exalted, He is a free agent, powerful, wise, disposer by power and choice. And He sees i.e., He the Glorified, as His statement: 'Does he not know that God sees?' [Surah Al-Alaq: 14]. Not like our sight. And He hears not like our hearing. For we see shapes and various colors and hear sounds and composed words by created instruments in composite limbs, in accordance with His enabling us to see and hear, as came in the supplication: 'O God, let us benefit from our hearing and our sight as long as You keep us alive.' And God the Glorified sees shapes, colors, and various forms with His sight which is His attribute, in the manner of His omnipotence, and He hears sounds, words, both simple and compound, with His hearing which is His attribute, without any instrument of instruments and without participation of any other being. And His seeing of visible things and His hearing of audible things are eternal in essence, even if the seen and heard are originated things, as has preceded in the explanation of the other attributes, that the later occurrence of the contingent relation does not negate the eternity of the eternal relation. Do you not see that you see in the state of sleep, by the powers of the inner parts of your brain, in the state of your dream, shapes and colors, and hear sounds and varieties, while no shape or color exists or is present, and after a past time you see those colors and shapes, and hear those sounds and words, in your waking state.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This is a detailed explanation of the attributes of knowledge, power, sight, and hearing, contrasting them with human attributes. The author follows the order of the matn. For each attribute, he first states the principle of incomparability, then elaborates. For knowledge: human knowledge is acquired through instruments and mental images, while God's knowledge is essential, self-subsistent, and comprehends all things. For power: human power is limited, instrumental, and delegated, while God's power is eternal, independent, and absolute. For sight and hearing: human sight and hearing are mediated by physical organs and perceive only present objects, while God's sight and hearing are eternal attributes, not dependent on instruments or the existence of objects. The author supports this with the dream analogy: in a dream, one sees shapes and hears sounds without any external object existing; similarly, God's seeing and hearing are not contingent upon the actual presence of things. This illustrates that God's attributes are not similar to ours even though they share the same names.

Key Terms
يعلم لا كعلمنا
يقدر لا كقدرتنا
يرى لا كرؤيتنا
يسمع لا كسمعنا
صفات ذاتية
متعلق حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the dream analogy shows God's attributes are similar to human powers because humans can also see and hear in dreams.
Correction: The analogy only demonstrates that God's sight and hearing are independent of external objects, not that they resemble human abilities. Human dream sight is still a created phenomenon, while God's attributes are eternal and uncreated.

Checkpoint
What does the author use the dream analogy to demonstrate?
A) That God's seeing and hearing are like human seeing and hearing.
B) That God's seeing and hearing do not require the existence of the seen or heard object.
C) That human sight is imperfect.
D) That dreams are proof of God's existence.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes of knowledge, power, sight, and hearing are absolute, eternal, and independent, while human attributes are limited, acquired, and instrumental.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Allah's Knowledge is Unlike Human Knowledge
The commentator contrasts human and divine knowledge, listing attributes of Allah's knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge is completely different in nature from human knowledge—it is essential, self-sufficient, and eternal, not acquired through any means.

Core Idea
Allah knows all things directly and eternally, unlike our limited, tool-dependent knowledge.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a fundamental aspect of Islamic theology: the nature of divine knowledge. He contrasts our human way of knowing—through tools, mental images, and limited understanding—with Allah's way of knowing, which is immediate, complete, and eternal. This lesson will help you grasp why divine knowledge is categorically different from human knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the key phrase 'not like our knowledge' sets the tone.
2
Identify the contrast
The passage explicitly contrasts human knowledge (using instruments and mental images) with Allah's knowledge (direct and essential). Underline the words that show this contrast.
3
Analyse the attributes of divine knowledge
Focus on the four attributes: essential (dhātī), self-sufficient (ṣamadī), beginningless (azalī), and endless (abadī). Consider what each means in relation to Allah.
These attributes are not mere adjectives—they define the nature of divine knowledge.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Why is it important that Allah's knowledge is not like ours? How does this shape our understanding of tawḥīd?
This connects to the core Islamic belief in Allah's perfection and uniqueness.

يعلم لا كعلمنا. كما بينه بقوله (يعلم) أي تعالى، كما في نسخة (لا) (كعلمنا أي معشر الخلق، فإنا نعلم الأشياء بآلات وتصور صور حاصلات في أذهاننا بقدر أفهامنا وإعلامنا، والله تعالى يعلم حقائق الأشياء كلّيها وجزئيها ظاهرها ومخفيها بعلم ذاتي صمدي أزلي أبدي.
He knows not like our knowledge. As he explained by his statement: He knows, meaning the Exalted, as in the copy: 'not like our knowledge' meaning of the community of creatures, for we know things by means of instruments and mental images that occur in our minds to the extent of our understanding and learning, while Allah the Exalted knows the realities of things, both universal and particular, apparent and hidden, with an eternal, self-sufficient, beginningless, and endless knowledge.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of knowledge (al-ʿilm) as it pertains to Allah and distinguishes it from human knowledge. The author begins by stating the lemma 'He knows not like our knowledge.' He then explains that we, the created beings, acquire knowledge through instruments (ālāt) and mental images (ṣuwar) that arise in our minds, limited by our capacity. In contrast, Allah knows the true realities of all things—both universal and particular, apparent and hidden—with a knowledge that is essential (dhātī), self-sufficient (ṣamadī), eternal without beginning (azalī), and eternal without end (abadī). This emphasizes that Allah's knowledge is not acquired through any means and is not limited by time or space.

Allah's Power is Unlike Human Power
The commentator explains that Allah's power is eternal and absolute, unlike human power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's power is completely different from human power in its nature, scope, and means.

Core Idea
Allah's power is eternal, without instruments, partners, or limits.

This lesson draws a sharp distinction between divine power and human power. While we rely on tools, helpers, and limited ability granted by Allah, His power is absolute, eternal, and self-sufficient. You'll explore the key attributes that make Allah's power unique.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noting the key terms. Try to sense the contrast being drawn between 'His power' and 'our power'.
Pay attention to the word 'la kaqudratina' – 'not like our power'.
2
Identify the attributes of Allah's power
The passage lists several characteristics of Allah's power: eternal, without instrument, without partnership, and over all things. Write them down.
These are qadima, bi-la alah, bi-la mushāraka, and 'ala kulli shay'in qadir.
3
Contrast with human power
Notice how human power is described: limited to some things, dependant on being given power (iqdar), and exercised through instruments and helpers.
This highlights our complete dependence on Allah.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters for theology. If Allah's power were like ours, He would be limited and need creation, but His power is absolute and independent.
This supports the Islamic concept of tawhid in attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقدر لا كقدرتنا. لأن قدرته تعالى قديمة لا بآلة ولا بمشاركة وهو على كل شيء قدير، ونحن لا نقدر إلا على بعض الأشياء بالإقدار، وذلك المقدار أيضاً بالآلات والأعوان والأنصار، وأما هو سبحانه وتعالى ففاعل مختار وقادر حكيم مدبّر بقدرة واختيار.
And He has power not like our power. Because His power, the Exalted, is eternal, not through an instrument nor with partnership, and He is over all things powerful. And we are not able except over some things by being given power, and that amount also is through instruments, helpers, and supporters. As for Him, the Glorified and Exalted, He is a free agent, powerful, wise, and disposer with power and choice.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of power (al-qudra) as it pertains to Allah. The lemma states 'He has power not like our power.' The explanation highlights that Allah's power is eternal (qadīma), not dependent on any instrument (ālāt) nor shared with any partner. Allah is capable of all things. In contrast, human power is limited; we can only do some things by receiving power (al-iqdār) from Allah, and that power is exercised through tools, helpers, and supporters. Allah, however, is a free agent (fāʿil mukhtār), powerful and wise, who disposes affairs through His own power and will.

Key Takeaway
Allah's power is absolute, eternal, and independent of any means, whereas human power is limited, derived, and reliant on instruments and support.

Allah's Seeing and Hearing: Eternal and Without Instruments
The commentator contrasts human and divine seeing/hearing and uses a dreaming analogy to show eternal perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes of sight and hearing are eternal, not dependent on the existence of objects, and are unlike human perception.

Core Idea
Allah's seeing and hearing are eternal, not dependent on what is seen or heard.

This passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar establishes a key principle about Allah's attributes: they are not like human attributes. Human sight and hearing depend on instruments and the presence of objects, but Allah's sight and hearing are eternal and do not require objects to exist for Him to perceive them. The author uses the analogy of dreaming to illustrate this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the contrast between 'not like our seeing' and the detailed explanation.
2
Contrast human and divine seeing
Identify how human seeing/hearing is described (instruments, created organs) versus divine seeing/hearing (attribute, without instruments).
3
Understand the dreaming analogy
The author uses the example of dreaming to show that one can perceive objects without them being present. Reflect on how this supports the idea that Allah's perception is eternal.
This analogy helps explain how Allah sees things before they exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويرى لا كرؤيتنا ويسمع لا كسمعنا. فإنا نرى الأشكال والألوان المختلفة ونسمع الأصوات والكلمات المؤتلفة بالآلات المخلوقة في الأعضاء المركبة على وفق إبصاره لأبصارنا وإسماعه لأسماعنا كما ورد في الدعا: ((اللهم متعنا بأسماعنا وأبصارنا ما أحييتنا)). والله سبحانه يرى الأشكال والألوان والهيئات المختلفة بإبصاره الذي هو صفته علی نعت اقتداره، ويسمع الأصوات والكلمات المفردات والمركبات بسمعه الذي هو نعته لا بآلة من الآلات ولا بمشاركة غيره من الكائنات، وإن رؤيته للمرئيات وسمعه للمسموعات قديمة بالذات وإن كان المرئي والمسموع من الحادثات على ما سبق بيانه من سائر الصفات من أن تأخر المتعلق الحادث لا ينافي تقدم المتعلق القديم ألا ترى أنك ترى في حالة نومك بقوى بطون دماغك في حالة رؤياك أشكالا وألوانا وتسمع أصواتا وأفنانا ولا شكل ولا لون بحاصل ولا حاضر وبعد زمان غابر ترى تلك الألون والأشكال، وتسمع تلك الأصوات والأقوال، في حال يقظتك على منوال ما رأيتها وسمعتها في تلك الحالة بلا زيادة ولا نقصان في المآل ومع الله الملك المتعال الموصوف بنعوت الكمال أنه كيف يرى الألون والأشكال قبل وجودها وكيف يسمع الأصوات والكلمات قبل وقوعها، وهو الذي يريك الأشكال والألوان في حالة نومك بدون حضورها، ويسمعك الأصوات والكلمات قبل صدورها.
And He sees not like our seeing, and He hears not like our hearing. For we see different shapes and colors and hear composite sounds and words by means of created instruments in compound organs, according to His giving us sight and hearing, as mentioned in the supplication: 'O Allah, let us enjoy our hearing and our sight as long as You keep us alive.' And Allah, Glorified is He, sees different shapes, colors, and forms with His sight which is His attribute in the manner of His power, and He hears sounds and words, simple and compound, with His hearing which is His attribute, not through any instrument nor with the participation of any other beings. And His seeing of visible things and His hearing of audible things are eternal in essence, even though the visible and audible are among temporal things, as previously explained regarding all attributes that the temporal nature of the contingent object does not contradict the precedence of the eternal attribute. Do you not see that you see in your sleep, by the powers of the inner parts of your brain during your dream, shapes and colors, and hear sounds and melodies, while no shape or color is actually present? Then after some time you see those colors and shapes and hear those sounds and words in your waking state, in the same manner as you saw and heard them in that state, without any increase or decrease. And if this is possible with God, the Sovereign, the Exalted, described with attributes of perfection, how does He see colors and shapes before their existence? And how does He hear sounds and words before their occurrence? And He is the One who shows you shapes and colors in your sleep without their presence, and makes you hear sounds and words before their occurrence.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage defines Allah's attributes of seeing (al-basar) and hearing (al-samʿ). The lemmata state 'He sees not like our seeing, and He hears not like our hearing.' The explanation begins by describing human sight and hearing: we see shapes and colors and hear sounds through created instruments in our bodily organs. This is by Allah's grace, as per the supplication. In contrast, Allah sees all forms and colors through His own sight attribute, and hears all sounds and words through His hearing attribute, without any instrument or partnership. Crucially, His seeing and hearing are eternal in essence (qadīma bi al-dhāt), even though the objects seen and heard are temporal. The author then provides an analogy: dreaming. In a dream, you can see shapes and colors and hear sounds even when no physical objects are present. Later, you may see those same things in reality. If this is possible in human dreams, then certainly Allah can see things before they exist and hear sounds before they occur, as He is the One who causes these perceptions. This refutes the notion that the attribute must be contemporary with its object.

يسمع
بصر
سمع
قديم بالذات
متعلق حادث

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Allah's seeing and hearing depend on the existence of objects, just as human perception does.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah's seeing and hearing are eternal and do not require the existence of objects; He sees and hears things before they occur, as shown by the dreaming analogy.

Checkpoint
How does the passage use the example of dreaming to explain Allah's seeing and hearing?
A) To show that human perception is unreliable.
B) To illustrate that one can perceive things that are not physically present, which is akin to Allah's eternal perception.
C) To argue that dreams are a form of divine revelation.
D) To prove that seeing requires an object.

Key Takeaway
Allah's sight and hearing are eternal attributes that do not depend on the existence of objects; He sees and hears all things before they occur.

?
Since Allah hears all sounds, including your silent thoughts, what is one thought you need to bring to Him in sincere repentance right now?

Allah's Speech: Without Instruments or Letters
Contrast between human and divine speech, affirming uncreatedness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental difference between Allah's speech and human speech: it is without instruments, letters, and is uncreated.

Core Idea
Allah speaks without organs or letters; His speech is uncreated and eternal.

In this lesson, we explore the nature of divine speech. The creed asserts that Allah speaks, but not like our speech. Our speech involves physical instruments and articulated letters. Allah's speech, however, is perfect and free from such limitations. It is uncreated and eternal in essence. This foundational distinction is crucial for understanding the Qur'an's divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the source passage up to 'قديم بالذات' to see the direct contrast between human and divine speech.
2
Identify the key differences
Notice the instruments: throat, tongue, lips, teeth, and the articulation of letters. Then contrast with Allah's speech: no instrument, no letters.
This establishes transcendence.
3
Reflect on the uncreatedness
The passage states letters are created, but Allah's speech is not created; rather it is eternal in essence. Ensure you grasp this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتكلم لا ككلامنا. كما بينه بقوله: ونحن نتكلم بالآلات أي من الحلق واللسان والشفة والأسنان والحروف أي الأصوات المعتمدة على المخارج المعهودات بالهيئات المعروفات والله تعالى يتكلم بلا آلة ولا حروف أي لكمالات الذات والصفات والحروف مخلوقة أي كالآلات وكلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق بل قديم بالذات قال الطحاوي: فمن سمعه فزعم أنه كلام البشر فقد كفر وقد ذمه الله وأوعده بسقر حيث قال تعالى: ﴿ سَأَصْلِيْهِ سَقَرَ ﴾ [المدثر : ٢٦] فلما أوعد الله بسقر لمن قال: ﴿ إِن هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ البَشَرِ [المدثر : ٢٥] علمنا وأيقنا أنه قول خالق البشر ولا يشبه قول البشر انتهى.
And He speaks not like our speech. As he explained by his statement: We speak by means of instruments, i.e., the throat, tongue, lips, and teeth, and letters, i.e., sounds based on known points of articulation according to recognized manners. And Allah the Exalted speaks without instrument or letters, i.e., due to the perfections of essence and attributes. And letters are created, i.e., like instruments, and the speech of Allah the Exalted is not created, rather eternal in essence. At-Tahawi said: Whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has disbelieved; Allah has censured him and threatened him with Saqar, as He said: 'I will cast him into Saqar.' Since Allah threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the word of a human,' we know with certainty that it is the speech of the Creator of humans, and it does not resemble the speech of humans. End.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of speech (al-kalām) for Allah. The lemma states 'He speaks not like our speech.' The commentary explains that human speech uses physical instruments (throat, tongue, lips, teeth) and letters (sounds from specific articulation points). In contrast, Allah speaks without any instrument or letters, due to the perfections of His essence and attributes. The letters themselves are created (makhlūqa), just like instruments. The speech of Allah, however, is uncreated (ghayr makhlūq) and eternal in essence (qadīm bi al-dhāt). The text then cites the authority of At-Tahawi, who states that claiming Allah's speech is human speech is disbelief (kufr), supported by the Qur'anic verses from Surat al-Muddaththir. This confirms that the Qur'an is the speech of the Creator, not resembling human speech.

Key Terms
كلام
حروف
مخلوق
غير مخلوق
قديم بالذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah's speech consists of letters and sounds like human speech.
Correction: This passage clarifies Allah speaks without any instrument or letter; His speech is uncreated and not composed of sounds.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Allah speak without instruments and letters?
A) Because He chooses not to use them.
B) Because of the perfections of His essence and attributes.
C) Because letters are evil.
D) Because He cannot speak in that manner.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is fundamentally different from human speech: it has no instruments, no letters, and is uncreated and eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you treat the words as merely human language, or do you actively remind yourself that you are engaging with the uncreated speech of Allah? How can you cultivate a deeper reverence in your recitation starting today?
?
If Allah's speech is without letters and instruments, then your mind cannot fully grasp it. Does this truth humble you, or do you still try to reduce Allah's attributes to fit your understanding? What specific habit can you change to submit to this mystery?
?
The claim that Allah's speech is created diminishes His perfection. Have you ever unconsciously lowered Allah in your heart by thinking of His speech as similar to yours? How will you guard against this in your daily worship and thoughts?

The Uncreated Speech and the Ruling of Disbelief
Ruling on claiming Allah's speech is human speech, with Qur'anic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that claiming Allah's speech is human speech constitutes disbelief, as established by At-Tahawi and the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Whoever says the Qur'an is human speech has disbelieved.

This lesson presents a stern warning from the early scholar At-Tahawi. He declares that anyone who hears the Qur'an and claims it is human speech becomes a disbeliever. He supports this with a Qur'anic verse that threatens such a person with the Fire of Saqar. This underscores the absolute conviction that the Qur'an is not created speech but the very word of the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'قال الطحاوي' to the end to understand the ruling and the evidence.
2
Identify the claim that causes disbelief
The claim is that Allah's speech (the Qur'an) is like human speech. Note the severe consequence.
3
Reflect on the evidence
At-Tahawi cites the verse from Surah al-Muddaththir where Allah threatens with Saqar those who say 'This is nothing but the word of a human.'
This provides the scriptural basis.

Divine Speech is Unlike Human Speech
Commentator explains that God's speech is unlike human speech and cites Tahawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine speech is fundamentally different from human speech, being uncreated and without instruments or letters.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal and uncreated, not composed of sounds or letters.

This passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar establishes a core theological distinction: Allah speaks, but not as we speak. Human speech depends on physical instruments and articulated sounds, while divine speech is an eternal attribute free from such limitations. The author emphasizes this by contrasting created letters with the uncreated speech of Allah, and reinforces the point with a warning from Imam al-Tahawi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the full theological statement. Notice how the text begins with the creedal phrase 'And He speaks not like our speech'.
2
Identify the contrast between human and divine speech
The passage explicitly contrasts human speech (instruments and letters) with divine speech (no instruments nor letters). Mark the phrases that define each.
3
Understand the status of letters
The text states that letters are created, while divine speech is uncreated (eternal). This is a key doctrinal point: the attribute of speech is eternal, but its verbal expression in creation is created.
4
Consider the Tahawi quote
Read the quote from Tahawi, which states that deeming divine speech as human speech is disbelief. The Quran verse is cited as evidence. Reflect on the gravity of this distinction.
5
Summarize the lesson
In your own words, write a brief summary of how the passage preserves divine transcendence regarding speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتكلم لا ككلامنا، ونحن نتكلم بالآلات والحروف، والله تعالى يتكلم بلا آلة ولا حروف، والحروف مخلوقة وكلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، هذا تتعجب على منوال ما رأيتها وسمعتها في تلك الحالة بلا زيادة ولا نقصان في المآل ومع الله الملك المتعال الموصوف بنعوت الكمال أنه كيف يرى الألون والأشكال قبل وجودها الأصوات والكلمات قبل وقوعها، وهو الذي يريك الأشكال والألوان في حالة نومك بدون حضورها، ويسمعك الأصوات والكلمات قبل صدورها. ويتكلم لا (ككلامنا كما بينه بقوله : ونحن نتكلم بالآلات) أي من الحلق واللسان والشفة والأسنان (والحروف) أي الأصوات المعتمدة على المخارج المعهودات بالهيئات المعروفات والله تعالى يتكلم بلا آلة ولا (حروف أي لكمالات الذات والصفات. والحروف (مخلوقة أي كالآلات وكلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق) بل قديم بالذات، قال الطحاوي: فمن سمعه فزعم أنه كلام البشر فقد كفر ، وقد ذمه الله وأوعده بسقر، حيث قال تعالى: ﴿ سَأَصْلِيْهِ سَقَرَ ﴾ [المدثر : ٢٦] ، فلما أوعد الله بسقر لمن قال: ﴿ إِن هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ البَشَرِ [المدثر : ٢٥] علمنا وأيقنا أنه قول خالق البشر، ولا يشبه قول البشر. انتهى.
And He speaks not like our speech. We speak with instruments and letters, while Allah the Exalted speaks without instrument or letters. Letters are created, and the speech of Allah the Exalted is uncreated. This is a wonder, upon the pattern of what you have seen and heard in that state without increase or decrease in the final outcome, and with Allah the King the Most High, described with attributes of perfection: how He sees colors and shapes before their existence, sounds and words before their occurrence, and He is the One who shows you shapes and colors in the state of your sleep without their presence, and makes you hear sounds and words before their issuance. And He speaks not (like our speech, as He explained by His saying: 'We speak with instruments') i.e., from the throat, tongue, lip, and teeth, (and letters) i.e., sounds dependent on the known points of articulation in the known forms. And Allah the Exalted speaks without instrument or (letters, i.e., for perfections of essence and attributes. And letters (are created i.e., like instruments) and the speech of Allah the Exalted is uncreated, nay, eternal by essence. Al-Tahawi said: So whoever hears it and claims it is human speech has disbelieved, and Allah has censured him and threatened him with Saqar, where He said Exalted: 'I will burn him in Saqar' [74:26]. When Allah threatened Saqar for the one who said 'This is nothing but the word of a human' [74:25], we knew and were certain that it is the word of the Creator of humans, and it does not resemble the speech of humans. End.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a definition and affirmation of the nature of divine speech as distinct from human speech. It begins by quoting the original text from Fiqh al-Akbar: 'And He speaks not like our speech.' The commentator then explains that humans speak using physical instruments (throat, tongue, lips, teeth) and letters (sounds produced from articulatory points), whereas Allah speaks without any instrument or letters. Letters are created, while Allah's speech is uncreated, eternal by essence. The passage then inserts a remark about the wonder of Allah's seeing and hearing before things exist, emphasizing that He perceives without tools. Then returns to the speech topic, reinforcing that Allah's speech is not like human speech, and quotes al-Tahawi who warns that deeming it human speech is disbelief, citing the Quranic threat against those who called it 'the word of a human.' The conclusion is that divine speech is the speech of the Creator, unlike the speech of creation. The commentator preserves the theological nuance that letters and instruments are created, while the attribute of speech is eternal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's speech resembles human speech in being composed of sounds and letters.
Correction: Divine speech is an eternal attribute without instruments or letters; letters and sounds are created.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of letters (حروف) in relation to divine speech?
A) Letters are eternal and uncreated like divine speech.
B) Letters are created, while divine speech is uncreated.
C) Letters are the same as divine speech.
D) Letters are instruments of divine speech.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute of Allah, fundamentally unlike human speech which involves instruments and created letters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you see it as the eternal speech of Allah or merely as words on a page? How does your current attitude affect your reverence and concentration during recitation? What will you change today to better honor the uncreated speech of your Lord?
?
The lesson teaches that Allah's speech is not like human speech—it is without letters or sounds. Yet we interact with the Quran through letters and sounds. How can you move beyond the physical form to connect with the divine essence? What practical steps can you take to listen to the Quran with the awareness that it is directly from Allah, not from a human author?
?
Reflect on the warning of Tahawi: claiming that the Quran is human speech leads to disbelief. Have you ever treated the Quran as a human product in your heart—doubting its divine origin, or prioritizing human scholarship over its message? Repent and commit to reading the Quran as the living word of the Eternal.
